### ⭐ [Long-lived local quantum coherences from hydrodynamic large deviations](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27074v1)

**Highlighted author(s):** Sarang Gopalakrishnan  
**Authors:** Ewan McCulloch, J. Alexander Jacoby, Sarang Gopalakrishnan  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27074v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `non-equilibrium dynamics` **4/5** · `entanglement & information structure` **3/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **3/5** · `non-equilibrium universality` **3/5** · `scars & prethermalization` **3/5** · `driven-dissipative phase transition` **2/5**

<sub>FIG. 4. Weak noise coherence–void polaron translation mode. (a) Mean-squared displacements of the coherence, ⟨X(t)2⟩, and of the void center of mass, ⟨xcom(t)2⟩, for several values of γ. At early times the coherence moves rapidly inside an already well-polarized quasi-stationary void, while the void center of mass diffuses much more slowly. At later times the coherence motion crosses over to match the void center of mass, indicating binding of the coherence to the slow polaron coordinate. <details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2604.27074_figures/2604.27074_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 5. Internal motion of the weak noise coherence– void polaron. (a) Mean-squared displacement of the relative-coordinate of the coherence and the void center-of- mass, ⟨(X(t) −xcom(t))2⟩, for γ = 0.007, 0.01, . . . , 0.1. In each case the relative-coordinate MSD approaches a late-time plateau, showing that the coherence remains confined inside the void, with the confinement length increasing as γ is re- duced. (b) Plateau value ℓ2 X(γ), extracted from the late-time relative-coordinate MSD, plotted against γ−2/3. The near- linear dependence is consistent with the Feynman-polaron prediction ℓζ ∼γ−1/3. These data are obtained from the same dilute-coherence population-dynamics sampling as in...</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** The paper describes how local quantum coherences in charge-conserving systems are protected by rare, low-entropy fluctuations known as 'voids.' This interaction creates a polaron-like object that significantly extends the lifetime of coherences and leads to non-trivial subdiffusive dynamics.

**Why it may be interesting.** This paper is highly relevant to many-body dynamics and open quantum systems as it provides a new mechanism for the protection of quantum information (coherence) via the formation of hydrodynamic 'voids' in the presence of noise.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Understanding how local quantum coherences between different charge sectors evolve and decay under generic charge-conserving dynamics, specifically investigating how they interact with hydrodynamic large deviations.

**Main result.** The authors show that quantum coherences form a collective 'void-coherence polaron' with surrounding charge-depleted regions, leading to parametrically enhanced lifetimes and subdiffusive dynamics in the noiseless limit.

**Method.** The study integrates local coherence dynamics into Macroscopic Flutuation Theory (MFT), using a path-integral approach over operator histories, a Feynman-style variational ansatz, and tensor-network simulations.

**Model / system.** Generic many-body quantum systems with a conserved U(1) charge, including 1D random charge-conserving circuits, the Symmetric Simple Exclusion Process (SSEP), and the Katz-Lebowitz-Spohn (KLS) model.

**Key observables.** Single-particle Green's function, autocorrelation functions of off-diagonal operators (e.g., sigma plus), spectral gap of the quantum channel, and many-body weight (MBW) distributions.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Noise strength (gamma), diffusion constant (D), charge density, and the integrability-breaking parameter (delta).

**Assumptions / limitations.** Assumes the ability to expand Heisenberg evolution into a suitable operator basis and assumes the diffusion constant remains finite at all densities.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 illustrates the low-entropy void structure in noisy and noiseless regimes; Figure 10 shows the variance of coherence position and time-dependent diffusion constants; Figure 12/13 show magnon number conservation breakdown and MBW evolution.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of coherence decay, develops a framework linking it to hydrodynamic large deviations, presents the 'polaron' model, provides analytical derivations for the weak-noise and noiseless limits, and validates results via numerical tensor-network simulations.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We develop a framework to describe how quantum coherences between distinct charge sectors evolve under generic charge-conserving dynamics. Our framework captures the nonperturbative interactions between quantum coherences and hydrodynamic large deviations -- i.e., rare ``voids'' of low charge entropy. Conditional on surviving, the quantum coherence and its surrounding void form a collective polaron-like object. In one dimension, even at infinite temperature, we show that the lifetime of coherences is parametrically enhanced because they bind to voids. We use our framework to address two fundamental questions about generic quantum dynamics with a conserved charge. First, we argue that gapped Ruelle-Pollicott resonances are absent in the weak-noise limit, even in sectors of operator space that contain no hydrodynamic slow modes: instead, the spectral gap in all sectors vanishes nonperturbatively in the noise strength. Second, we compute the spacetime asymptotics of the dynamical single-particle Green's function, both in the weak-noise regime and in the absence of noise. In the noiseless case, we find that the void-coherence polaron undergoes subdiffusion, with an exponent we calculate. We support our general arguments with a microscopic derivation for random charge-conserving circuits, as well as numerical evidence from tensor-network simulations.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

### ⭐ [Observation of Vinen turbulence during far-from-equilibrium Bose-Einstein condensation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.28191v1)

**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `non-equilibrium dynamics` **4/5** · 🔥 `non-equilibrium universality` **4/5**

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2604.28191_figures/2604.28191_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 5. Universality of Vinen turbulence, for varying a (set at t = 0). (a) The evolution of L for different a is always fit well (solid lines) by Eq. (4), with only the non-universal t∗depending on a. Here, all three data sets are fit with the same B = 1.0(1)ℏ/m; fitting them independently gives consistent B values. Accounting for the difference in the particle mass, this value of B is essentially the same as obtained for superfluid helium [65]. (b) Plotting the same data according to Eq. (4), with a-dependent t∗, collapses them onto the same universal curve; the solid line corresponds to B = 1.0ℏ/m. The dashed line shows the exponential with timescale 300ms that coincides with the solid...</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper reports the direct observation of decaying quantum turbulence in a 3D Bose-Einstein condensate. By measuring the decay of vortex line density, the authors show that the system follows universal Vinen turbulence dynamics, where the decay rate is independent of the interatomic interaction strength.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work demonstrates universal hydrodynamic behavior and scaling laws in a highly compressible quantum gas, providing a bridge between ultracold atom experiments and the physics of strongly interacting superfluid Helium.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Understanding the relaxation dynamics and the emergence of long-range order in far-from-equilibrium quantum fluids, specifically the decay of a turbulent tangle of vortex lines.

**Main result.** The researchers observed the decay of vortex line-length density in a 3D Bose gas and found it follows the prediction for Vinen 'ultraquantum' turbulence, with a decay prefactor B that is universal and independent of interaction strength.

**Method.** The team used matter-wave magnification via a pulsed harmonic potential to enlarge the gas density distribution and imaged a thin slice of the cloud to identify vortex imprints as density dips.

**Model / system.** A homogeneous 3D atomic Bose gas of 39K atoms trapped in a cylindrical optical box trap, prepared in a far-from-equilibrium state by initiating interactions via Feshbach resonance.

**Key observables.** Vortex line-length density (L), coherence length (l), and the decay constant (B).

**Important parameters / regimes.** S-wave scattering length (a), vortex core size (healing length xi), and the decay timescale (tau).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The large-scale dynamics of the highly compressible gas can be treated as an incompressible hydrodynamic fluid.

**Figures summary.** Fig 1 shows the experimental concept of vortex tangle decay and magnification; Fig 2 displays the temporal evolution of density fluctuations into vortices and the evolution of coherence length; Fig 3 visualizes the decay of vortex lines; Fig 4 and 5 demonstrate the quantification of vortex imprints and the fit to the Vinen decay model.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the experimental concept of vortex decay in a box trap, describes the imaging and magnification techniques, presents the temporal evolution of the gas and coherence length, quantifies the vortex line density, and compares the decay dynamics to the Vinen turbulence model and superfluid Helium.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Relaxation of far-from-equilibrium quantum fluids, intimately related to the emergence of long-range order, is theoretically associated with the decay of a turbulent isotropic tangle of vortex lines. We observe and study such decaying quantum turbulence in a homogeneous 3D atomic Bose gas. Using matter-wave techniques to magnify the gas density distribution, and then imaging a thin slice of the magnified cloud, we observe imprints of randomly oriented vortex lines and measure the vortex line-length density $\mathcal{L}$. The observed decay of $\mathcal{L}$ agrees with the prediction for Vinen `ultraquantum' turbulence. Although our weakly interacting gases are highly compressible, their large-scale dynamics are consistent with the behavior of an incompressible hydrodynamic fluid, with the decay of $\mathcal{L}$ not depending on the strength of the interatomic interactions and being similar to that in the strongly interacting superfluid helium.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

Unlike the transverse-field quench, here, nonanalytic be- havior in the time evolution of observables persists in the presence of dissipation. However, increasing the dis- sipation strength progressively smears out the dynamical phase transition [67]. In conclusion, our results demonstrate that,...</sub>

**Summary.** This paper explores how the nature of dissipation determines whether an open quantum system relaxes to a thermal-like state or a complex nonequilibrium state. By studying coupled quantum Ising models, the authors demonstrate that local dissipation can induce a unique reentrant phase transition. This work highlights the critical role of dissipative mechanisms in shaping the phase diagrams of many-body systems.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides fundamental insights into how the specific structure of system-environment coupling can qualitatively change the phase structure and critical behavior of many-body open quantum systems.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating how different dissipative mechanisms (detailed balance vs. local pump-loss) control the emergence of equilibrium-like versus genuinely nonequilibrium critical behavior and phase transitions in open quantum systems.

**Main result.** The study finds that while detailed-balance dissipation leads to steady states resembling thermal Gibbs states, local spin-operator dissipation creates a richer nonequilibrium phase diagram featuring a reentrant symmetry-broken phase.

**Method.** The authors use a self-consistent mean-field approach to solve a nonlinear Lindblad master equation, employing linear stability analysis and numerical integration to characterize phase transitions and relaxation dynamics.

**Model / system.** Two coupled, fully connected (all-to-all) quantum Ising models governed by a nonlinear Lindblad master equation that includes both coherent unitary evolution and incoherent dissipative processes.

**Key observables.** Magnetization (order parameter), inter-model correlation functions, mixed-state fidelity, fidelity rate function, and quantum Fisher information.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Transverse field strengths (h1, h2), inter-model coupling (lambda), bath temperature (T), and system-bath coupling strength (gamma).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The system is treated in the thermodynamic limit using a mean-field approximation, and the environment is assumed to be Markovian (memoryless).

**Figures summary.** Figures show post-quench fidelity and magnetization dynamics, the phase diagram in the h1-gamma plane, the stability gap, and bifurcation diagrams illustrating the emergence of symmetry-broken phases.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the model and dissipative classes, analyzes relaxation dynamics following parameter quenches, explores steady-state phase diagrams for different dissipators, and concludes with a comparison of equilibrium-like vs. nonequilibrium criticality.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We study dissipative phase transitions in a system of two coupled fully-connected quantum Ising models interacting with an environment. The dynamics is governed by a Lindblad master equation combining coherent unitary evolution and incoherent dissipative processes, where the unitary part is described within a self-consistent mean-field framework effectively acting on the local Hilbert space of two coupled spins at each site.   We analyze two fundamentally different classes of dissipators. In the first case, the jump operators are defined in the instantaneous eigenbasis of the mean-field Hamiltonian and satisfy a detailed-balance condition. In this setting, the relaxation dynamics depends strongly on the quench protocol: a parametric quench of the Hamiltonian leads to conventional relaxation, whereas a temperature quench gives rise to a dynamical phase transition characterized by nonanalytic behavior in time. Yet, in both cases, the system relaxes toward a steady state determined solely by the post-quench parameters and the bath temperature, which closely resembles a thermal Gibbs state of the mean-field Hamiltonian. As a result, the dissipative phase transition occurs at a critical point consistent with the corresponding equilibrium transition. In contrast, when the dissipators are realized via local spin raising and lowering operators, the steady state is genuinely nonequilibrium, leading to a significantly richer phase diagram. In particular, for sufficiently strong system-bath coupling, we observe a reentrant phase featuring a symmetry-broken region bounded by two continuous dissipative phase transitions.   Our results evidence how the structure of dissipative processes controls the emergence of equilibrium-like versus genuinely nonequilibrium critical behavior in open quantum systems.

</details>

### [Quantum Magnetometry with Orientation beyond Steady-State Limits in Cavity-Magnon Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27608v1)

**Summary.** This paper proposes a new way to use the short-term 'transient' behavior of cavity-magnon systems to detect magnetic fields with much higher precision than steady-state methods. By carefully preparing the system's initial state and using squeezed light, the researchers show it is possible to reconstruct the full 3D direction of a magnetic field while canceling out unwanted quantum noise.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a sophisticated application of open quantum systems theory, specifically regarding how non-equilibrium transient dynamics and engineered initial states can be leveraged to bypass fundamental quantum noise limits in sensing.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Conventional steady-state cavity-magnon magnetometry is limited by the loss of initial-state quantum information, an inability to detect 3D magnetic field orientations, and sensitivity limits imposed by cavity-added quantum noise.

**Main result.** The authors demonstrate a transient sensing framework that uses pre-engineered initial states and squeezing to enhance SNR, enables crosstalk-free 3D magnetic field reconstruction, and identifies a resonance condition for full cavity-noise cancellation.

**Method.** The study employs Heisenberg-Langevin equations and input-output relations to analyze finite-time dynamics, utilizing a double-difference scheme for vectorial reconstruction and injected squeezed reservoirs for noise suppression.

**Model / system.** A cavity-magnon system consisting of a microwave cavity coupled to one or more Yttrium Iron Garnet (YIG) spheres, modeled via a Hamiltonian including cavity-magnon coupling, Zeeman interaction, and transverse magnetic drives.

**Key observables.** Cavity field amplitude and phase quadratures, Signal-to-Noise Ratio (SNR), and the 3D magnetic field vector components (azimuthal and polar angles).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Coupling strength (g_am), cavity and magnon decay rates (kappa_a, kappa_m), squeezing amplitude (r), measurement time (t_m), and number of YIG spheres (N).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The magnetic field signal is assumed to be a weak delta-function pulse, and the system operates in the weak-coupling regime.

**Figures summary.** Figure 2 shows SNR vs. frequency and resonant SNR; Figure 5 illustrates stationary SNR versus frequency for various squeezing levels and SNR as a function of temperature and squeezing.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the limitations of steady-state sensing, presents a transient framework for 3D reconstruction, analyzes noise suppression via squeezing and resonance, and discusses scalability using YIG arrays.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We present a transient quantum sensing framework for cavity-magnon systems that circumvents the inevitable loss of initial-state quantum properties plaguing conventional steady-state protocols. Explicitly incorporating finite-time dynamics and adopting an engineered steady state as the initial condition, we derive the exact transient noise spectrum. We show that residual initial quantum correlations alone can drastically enhance the short-time signal-to-noise ratio (SNR) beyond that achievable with unsqueezed steady-state schemes. Through analysis of the transient spectral density and joint measurements of orthogonal cavity quadratures, we realize crosstalk-free reconstruction of all three magnetic field components, enabling orientation of magnetic signals. In the long-time limit, our theory yields a closed-form stationary noise spectrum and uncovers a resonance condition $g_{am}=\sqrt{κ_aκ_m}/2$, where cavity field quantum noise is fully canceled without requiring strong coherent coupling. Away from this resonance, injected squeezing further suppresses cavity induced noise and broadens the detection bandwidth. Extending the framework to an array of $N$ yttrium iron garnet (YIG) spheres generates a collective bright mode, with magnon-probe noise scaling as $1/N$. Our results establish a unified route to scalable, high precision, multidimensional quantum magnetometry using cavity-magnon platforms.

</details>

**Summary.** This paper introduces a framework to characterize errors in measurement-conditioned operations in dynamic quantum circuits by analyzing individual measurement branches. Using the IBM Fez processor, the authors show that the best error mitigation strategy depends on the underlying readout noise of the hardware. This branch-resolved approach reveals critical error structures that are otherwise obscured by traditional outcome-averaged analysis.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a sophisticated framework for analyzing non-trace-preserving dynamics in open quantum systems and demonstrates how branch-specific noise analysis can outperform standard aggregate-state fidelity metrics.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Characterizing the 'feed-forward error' in dynamic quantum circuits, specifically how measurement-conditioned corrective operations behave across individual measurement branches rather than just in aggregate.

**Main result.** The study demonstrates that the effectiveness of error mitigation strategies (PROM vs. post-processing) depends on the hardware's readout error profile, and that branch-resolved analysis reveals error structures hidden by outcome-averaged metrics.

**Method.** The authors use 'Classical Choi Shadows' to reconstruct branch-resolved Choi operators and validate them against full tomography, evaluating three correction strategies: physical application, post-processing, and PROM-based mitigation.

**Model / system.** The experiment is performed on the IBM 'Fez' (Heron r2) superconducting quantum processor using a 6-qubit logical setup for single-qubit teleportation with W4 resource states.

**Key observables.** Branch Choi operators, branch quality (overlap with ideal state), feed-forward penalty, and readout assignment error (RAE).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Readout error levels (high vs. low), branch-specific probabilities, and the use of bit-flip averaging (B5A) for mitigation.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis assumes the mid-circuit measurement can be modeled as a quantum instrument with discrete branches, and uses a fixed transpilation seed for reproducibility.

**Figures summary.** Fig 1 shows the teleportation workflow and estimation framework; Fig 2 and 3 detail the circuit for state preparation and decoding; Fig 4 validates shadow estimator accuracy; Fig 5 and 6 compare branch quality across different correction strategies and layouts; Fig 7 shows aggregated error metrics.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of feed-forward error, defines the mathematical framework for branch-resolved characterization, describes the experimental setup and correction strategies, presents validation of the shadow estimator, and concludes with a comparative analysis of mitigation performance across different hardware layouts.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Mid-circuit measurement and classical feed-forward are essential primitives for dynamic-circuit teleportation on superconducting quantum processors. However, the error associated with measurement-conditioned corrective operations remains poorly understood when evaluated with respect to individual measurement branches. In this paper, we present a framework for characterizing feed-forward error in dynamic circuit teleportation without losing valuable information related to its behavior across separate branches. We analyze three approaches to applying measurement-conditioned corrections: (i) physical application, (ii) post-processing adjustments, and (iii) a mitigated physical application which utilizes Bit-Flip Averaging (BFA)-based Probabilistic Readout Error Mitigation (PROM). We experimentally reconstruct branch Choi operators via an entangled reference qubit, and validate our physical-application and post-processing Choi-shadow estimators against full tomography of the branch Choi operators. We perform experiments on two physical qubit layouts which differ greatly in mid-circuit measurement readout error, and observe a reversal in the relative order in branch qualities obtained from the post-processing and PROM mitigation strategies. In one physical layout with higher measurement readout error, the operational feed-forward penalty is relatively modest (approximately 0.02-0.03) and PROM produces higher branch qualities than post-processing for every branch. In a separate layout with lower readout error, the operational feed-forward penalty increases to roughly 0.07, and post-processing exceeds PROM for all branch qualities. Our characterization framework can reveal branch-specific error structure and mitigation behavior that state-of-the-art outcome-averaged analyses fail to expose.

</details>

**Summary.** This paper presents a method to implement Simon's algorithm with constant-depth circuits on NISQ hardware by using a hardware-aware compilation strategy. By reducing circuit depth, the authors successfully demonstrated exponential quantum speedup on large-scale superconducting processors.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Demonstrating exponential quantum speedup for a version of Simon's problem on NISQ-era superconducting hardware while overcoming high circuit depth and SWAP overhead.

**Main result.** The authors achieved exponential speedup on the 156-qubit 'Boston' processor and both exponential and polynomial speedup on the 120-qubit 'Miami' processor using a constant-depth compilation strategy.

**Method.** A hardware-aware compilation strategy that reduces the quantum part of Simon queries to $O(1)$ depth and a Bayesian post-processing algorithm to identify the hidden bitstring.

**Model / system.** Superconducting quantum processors from IBM, specifically the 15FR-qubit 'Boston' (heavy-hex connectivity) and 120-qubit 'Miami' (square-lattice connectivity) devices.

**Key observables.** Number-of-queries-to-solution (NTS), NTS for ideal quantum (NTS_IQ), and scaling exponents (alpha for polylog, beta for poly).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Hamming weight (w) of the hidden bitstring, problem size (n), and the use of the Akaike Information Criterion (AIC) for model selection.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The speedup is demonstrated for a restricted-Hamming-weight version of Simon's problem; comparison is made against a theoretical classical lower bound rather than an optimal classical player.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate the quantum circuit construction, the comparison of oracle methods, scaling plots of NTS vs. problem size/Hamming weight, and statistical diagnostics (AIC/R2) for model comparison.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem and circuit construction, details the hardware-aware compilation method, presents experimental results on two IBM processors, performs statistical scaling analysis to distinguish between exponential and polynomial speedup, and discusses the impact of error mitigation tools.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We demonstrate exponential quantum speedup for a restricted-Hamming-weight version of Simon's problem on present-day superconducting quantum processors by introducing a hardware-aware compilation strategy that compiles the quantum part of each Simon query circuit to constant depth. The resulting compiled circuits have $O(1)$ depth and linear connectivity, map directly onto common device layouts, and avoid additional routing and SWAP overhead. Implemented on IBM's $156$-qubit Boston and $120$-qubit Miami processors, the resulting circuits achieve sufficiently high fidelity to exhibit algorithmic quantum speedup without error suppression. Using the number-of-queries-to-solution metric, we observe exponential speedup over the classical lower bound across the full Hamming-weight range studied on Boston and across low-to-intermediate Hamming weights on Miami; at higher Hamming weights on Miami, we still observe polynomial speedup. The same construction also reaches a regime where the original Simon problem is recovered for the problem sizes studied. These results show that careful hardware-aware compilation can make exponential quantum speedup experimentally accessible for a canonical hidden-subgroup problem in the NISQ regime.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.28151"></a>
### [Domain-wall melting in all-to-all QSSEP from random-matrix theory](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.28151v1)

**Authors:** Denis Bernard, Lorenzo Piroli, Stefano Scopa  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.28151v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `entanglement & information structure` **4/5** · 🔥 `non-equilibrium dynamics` **4/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **3/5** · `non-equilibrium universality` **3/5** · `driven-dissipative phase transition` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2604.28151_figures/2604.28151_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 1. Illustration of the setup. We consider a one-dimensional quantum system of size L, where spinless fermions can hop between any pair of sites j →k, with amplitudes given by different realization of the complex Brownian motion. The hopping amplitudes are reset at each time step. The system is initialized in a domain-wall configuration, with the leftmost M sites occupied and the rest of the chain empty. During the evolution, we probe fluctuations in a subregion Aℓof size ℓ.</sub>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2604.28151_figures/2604.28151_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 2. Entropy density dynamics from a domain-wall initial state with L = 32 and M = ℓ= L/2. The solid line corresponds to the analytic prediction in Eq. (46), while the symbols are obtained from numerical simulations of the quantum dynamics (see Appendix A), averaged over 200 realizations. The dashed horizontal line marks the steady-state value s(∞) = 2 log(2) −1.</sub>

**Summary.** This paper provides an exact analytical description of how a domain wall melts in the all-to-all quantum symmetric simple exclusion process. By using random matrix theory, the authors show that entanglement entropy and particle fluctuations can be calculated explicitly and that quantum and classical transport statistics become identical in the thermodynamic limit.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides an exact analytical framework for studying non-equilibrium dynamics and entanglement growth in many-body systems with long-range interactions, bridging the gap between quantum and classical stochastic transport.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Characterizing the real-time dynamics of coherent quantum fluctuations and particle transport during the melting of an initial domain wall in an all-to-all quantum system.

**Main result.** The authors show that the eigenvalues of the correlation matrix follow a Jacobi process, leading to an explicit analytical expression for entanglement entropy and demonstrating that quantum and classical full-counting statistics coincide in the thermodynamic limit.

**Method.** The study utilizes Random Matrix Theory (RMT), Ito calculus, and stochastic differential equations (SDEs) to map the dynamics to a Jacobi process and derive exact evolution equations.

**Model / system.** The model is the all-to-all Quantum Symmetric Simple Exclusion Process (QSSEP), also known as the charged SYK2 model, consisting of L fermionic modes with hopping driven by complex Brownian motion.

**Key observables.** von Neumann entanglement entropy, Rényi entropy, and full-counting statistics (FCS) of the charge.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Thermodynamic limit (L approaching infinity), subsystem size (l), particle number (M), and the ratio of subsystem to system size (theta).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analytical solution for entropy is derived for the specific case where the domain wall splits the system into two equal halves; the self-averaging property assumes certain boundedness of the derivatives of the observable functions.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the 1D all-to-all hopping setup; Figure 2 compares numerical entropy dynamics with analytical predictions; Figure 3 shows charge full-counting statistics; Figure 5 illustrates the L^-1 scaling of finite-size deviations.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the all-to-all QSSEP model, applies RMT to identify the Jacobi process for eigenvalue evolution, derives analytical expressions for entanglement and charge statistics, performs finite-size scaling analysis, and concludes with a proof of self-averaging.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We study the melting of a domain wall in the quantum simple exclusion process with all-to-all hoppings (a.k.a. the charged SYK$_2$ model). We show that the real-time dynamics of physical quantities of interest can be obtained exploiting spectral results in random matrix theory. We first show that the eigenvalues of the correlation matrix corresponding to the initially charged subsystem evolve according to a Jacobi process, which is defined in terms of a closed system of stochastic differential equations. In turn, this observation allows us to obtain the real-time dynamics of all the eigenvalue moments. We present two physical applications. First, we study the dynamics of the averaged von Neumann entanglement entropy, arriving at a fully explicit expression in the thermodynamic limit. Second, we compute analytically the full-counting statistics of the charge. Our formula allows us to perform a thorough comparison with the full-counting statistics of the classical simple exclusion process. Notably, we show that, in the thermodynamic limit, the quantum and classical full-counting statistics coincide, with no finite-time corrections.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27250"></a>
### [Emergence of prethermal time quasicrystalline order in a quasiperiodically driven non-interacting spin chain](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27250v1)

**Authors:** Davood Marripour, Jahanfar Abouie  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** disordered systems and neural networks · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27250v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `non-equilibrium dynamics` **4/5** · 🔥 `scars & prethermalization` **4/5** · `driven-dissipative phase transition` **3/5** · `entanglement & information structure` **3/5**

**Summary.** This paper demonstrates that a spin chain driven by two incommensurate frequencies can exhibit a stable, prethermal time quasicrystalline phase. The researchers show that this phase features quasiperiodic time-translation symmetry breaking and is resistant to heating. The findings highlight how the interplay of disorder and quasiperiodic driving can create long-lived nonequilibrium states.

**Why it may be interesting.** It explores the intersection of quasiperiodic driving and disorder to create a new type of temporal order (TQC) that extends beyond standard Floquet-based discrete time crystals, offering insights into many-body dynamics and heating suppression.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The study investigates the emergence and stability of prethermal time quasicrystalline (TQC) order in a spin chain subjected to quasiperiodic driving.

**Main result.** The authors demonstrate that quasiperiodic driving leads to quasiperiodic time-translation symmetry breaking (QTTSB) with robust spectral peaks at incommensurate frequencies and a suppressed heating regime characterized by a prethermal entanglement entropy plateau.

**Method.** The study employs exact diagonalization to analyze the dynamics of the spin chain.

**Model / system.** A non-interacting spin-1/2 chain with disordered Ising interactions (randomly chosen from a symmetric interval) and a random transverse field, driven by a two-part periodic process involving a rotating transverse magnetic field at an incommensurate frequency ratio.

**Key observables.** Time autocorrelation function, dynamical structure factor, and entanglement entropy (EE).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Driving frequencies (omega_d and Omega), the irrational ratio omega_d/Omega, the high-frequency regime, and the asymmetry of the Ising exchange coupling distribution.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The system is treated as a non-interacting spin chain; the study focuses on the high-frequency regime to observe prethermal effects.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the quasiperiodically driven model, describes the numerical methodology using exact diagonalization, presents results for spectral features and entanglement entropy, analyzes the effects of disorder asymmetry and perturbations, and concludes with the implications for nonequilibrium temporal order.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We study prethermal time quasicrystalline (TQC) order in a quasiperiodically driven chain of non-interacting spin-1/2 particles. The drive consists of two parts, switched on and off periodically with frequency $ω_d$: (i) disordered Ising interactions, with exchange couplings chosen from a symmetric interval $[-J/2, J/2]$, allowing random antiferromagnetic or ferromagnetic nearest-neighbor couplings, together with a random transverse field; and (ii) a rotating transverse magnetic field with frequency $Ω$.   The ratio $ω_d/Ω$ is chosen to be irrational, producing multiple incommensurate frequencies and yielding quasiperiodic dynamics beyond Floquet theory. Using exact diagonalization, we analyze the time autocorrelation function, dynamical structure factor, and entanglement entropy (EE). In the high-frequency regime, robust spectral peaks at incommensurate frequencies (not integer multiples of the fundamental drives) signal quasiperiodic time-translation symmetry breaking (QTTSB). The EE exhibits sublinear power-law growth followed by a prethermal plateau, indicating suppressed resonant heating due to an energy scale mismatch. The nonequilibrium lifetime increases rapidly with driving frequency. Unlike symmetric disorder sampling, an asymmetric distribution of the Ising exchange couplings induces collective spin rigidity, enhancing the system's resistance to heating. The TQC phase remains stable against next-nearest-neighbor (NNN) exchange perturbations and rotational imperfections, with robustness comparable to discrete time crystals (TCs) under periodic driving. Our results establish this quasiperiodically driven system as a platform for long-lived nonequilibrium temporal order, revealing the interplay of disorder, collective rigidity, and quasiperiodic driving.

</details>

### [Experimental detection of entanglement in multimode Gaussian states from high-order intensity correlation moments](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27567v1)

**Summary.** This paper presents a method to experimentally detect entanglement in multi-mode Gaussian states using only high-order intensity correlations. By using mathematical bounds to overcome the lack of phase information, the authors successfully certify entanglement in both two-mode and three-mode squeezed states using a multiplexed SNSPD detector.

**Why it may be interesting.** This is highly relevant to quantum optics and quantum information as it provides a robust, phase-insensitive protocol for certifying entanglement in complex multi-mode Gaussian states, which is critical for scalable photonic quantum networks.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The challenge of detecting entanglement in multi-mode Gaussian states without the need for a coherent local oscillator or phase reference, which are typically required for homodyne-based detection.

**Main result.** The authors experimentally demonstrated the detection of entanglement in two-mode and three-mode Gaussian states using high-order intensity correlation moments, establishing a method that works even when phase information is unavailable.

**Method.** The researchers used symplectic quantum universal invariants (QUIs) derived from intensity correlation moments and applied the Peres-Horodecki (PPT) criterion, using mathematical bounding techniques to account for missing phase information in the three-mode case.

**Model / system.** The experimental platform uses spontaneous and cascaded parametric down-conversion (SPDC) in customized KTiOPO4 crystals, driven by a high-peak-energy pulsed laser, and employs a 32-channel pseudo-photon-number-resolving detector made of multiplexed SNSPDs.

**Key observables.** High-order intensity correlation moments (up to sixth-order), including $g^{(2)}_{12}$, $g^{(4)}_{12}$, and mean photon numbers.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Squeezing parameters (r), pump laser purity ($g^{(2)}(0)$), and the smallest symplectic eigenvalue ($	ilde{\lambda}_-$).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The states are assumed to be Gaussian; the derivation for TMSV assumes the state satisfies $\langle a_i angle = 0$ and $\langle a_i^2 angle = 0$; and the three-mode analysis requires using bounds due to the lack of phase-sensitive information.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the experimental setup for TMSV and TMGS generation; Figure 2 compares simulated and experimental PPT inequalities for TMSV; Figure 3 shows the effect of pump purity on symplectic eigenvalues; Figure 4 illustrates the PPT inequality bounds for TMGS.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of phase-insensitive entanglement detection, presents the theoretical derivation of intensity-based invariants and PPT bounds, describes the experimental setup for SPDC and PNR detection, and concludes with experimental verification of entanglement in two-mode and three-mode states.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Quantum universal invariants of a Gaussian state's covariance matrix, which can be derived from intensity correlation moments, have been adopted to characterize the entanglement properties of Gaussian states via the positive partial transpose criterion, also known as the Peres-Horodecki separability criterion. Such intensity correlation moments enable the extraction of information about the covariance matrix without the need for a coherent local oscillator. Here, we experimentally detect the entanglement properties of multimode Gaussian states using high-order\,(up to sixth-order) intensity correlation moments. These multimode Gaussian states are prepared via spontaneous and cascaded parametric down-conversion pumped by a high-peak-energy pulsed laser. Their intensity correlation moments are measured using a pseudo-photon-number-resolving detector constructed through spatial multiplexing of 32 threshold superconducting nanowire single photon detectors. This method is successfully demonstrated for two-mode and three-mode Gaussian states and can be extended to $N$-mode Gaussian states with $N>3$.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27585"></a>
### [Observation of Universal Spectral Moments and the Dynamic Dispersive-to-Proliferative Transition](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27585v1)

**Authors:** Jia-Xin Zhong, Chang Shu, Nan Cheng, Jee Woo Kim, Kai Zhang, Kai Sun, Yun Jing  
**Type:** both · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27585v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `driven-dissipative phase transition` **4/5** · 🔥 `non-equilibrium dynamics` **4/5** · `non-equilibrium universality` **3/5** · `analog quantum simulation` **2/5**

**Summary.** This paper shows that while the energy spectra of non-Hermitian systems change drastically with boundary conditions, their spectral moments remain stable and reflect true bulk properties. By using acoustic lattices, the authors demonstrate that these moments can predict a transition between stable dispersive dynamics and unstable proliferative dynamics. This provides a new way to characterize and control the behavior of non-Hermitian matter in finite-sized devices.

**Why it may be interesting.** It challenges the conventional view that PT-symmetry breaking necessarily leads to dynamical instability by showing that bulk dynamics can remain stable if governed by moment structure, which is highly relevant for controlling open quantum systems.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The sensitivity of spectra to boundary conditions in non-Hermitian systems (the skin effect) makes it difficult to identify boundary-robust bulk properties in finite-sized lattices.

**Main result.** The authors demonstrate that spectral moments serve as boundary-robust bulk observables and identify a dispersive-to-proliferative dynamical transition governed by these moments rather than spectral boundary sensitivity.

**Method.** The study uses a unified acoustic platform for full spectral reconstruction and time-domain access, combined with a newly developed loop-counting theory to quantify finite-size deviations.

**Model / system.** The experimental platform consists of 1D, 2D, and 3D acoustic lattices exhibiting non-Hermitian physics and the non-Hermitian skin effect.

**Key observables.** Spectral moments (one-, two-, and three-dimensional), complex spectra, and local bulk dynamics (dispersive vs. proliferative regimes).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Boundary geometries, lattice dimensionality, and the PT-broken regime.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The study relies on the connection between the thermodynamic theorem and finite systems via a loop-counting theory.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of boundary sensitivity in non-Hermitian spectra, presents experimental evidence of spectral moment invariance across geometries, introduces a loop-counting theory for finite-size corrections, and concludes with the discovery of a new dynamical transition.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

In non-Hermitian systems, spectra can be maximally boundary-sensitive, yet bulk physics need not be. Here we experimentally show that spectral moments provide boundary-robust bulk observables in finite non-Hermitian lattices, even when the spectra undergo dramatic geometry-dependent reshaping due to the skin effect. Using a unified acoustic platform with full spectral reconstruction and time-domain access, we probe one-, two- and three-dimensional lattices and demonstrate that spectral moments remain nearly invariant across distinct boundary geometries while the corresponding complex spectra differ strongly. To connect the thermodynamic theorem to realistic finite systems, we develop a loop-counting theory that identifies the physical origin of finite-size deviations in terms of missing boundary loops, quantitatively captures the corrections, and predicts a scaling law, which we verify experimentally. Beyond acoustic spectroscopy, we reveal a counterintuitive dynamical consequence of moment invariance: a dispersive-to-proliferative bulk transition governed by bulk moment structure rather than spectral boundary sensitivity. As a result, local bulk dynamics can remain stable (dispersive) even in a $\mathcal{PT}$-broken spectral regime, challenging the conventional expectation that $\mathcal{PT}$ breaking necessarily implies feedback-induced dynamical instability (proliferation) through exponentially amplifying spectral components. These results establish spectral moments as practical bulk descriptors for finite non-Hermitian matter and open a route to extracting and controlling intrinsic bulk behavior in realistic wave-based non-Hermitian devices.

</details>

### [Adaptable Continuous Variable Quantum Network with Finite Size Security](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27943v1)

**Authors:** Runjia Zhang, Akash nag Oruganti, Huy Q Nguyen, Adnan A. E. Hajomer, Vladyslav C. Usenko, Ulrik L. Andersen, Tobias Gehring

**Summary.** The researchers demonstrated a 1-to-4 continuous-variable quantum network that can adapt its security level based on user trust. By accounting for finite-size effects, they achieved high-performance secret key generation compatible with existing telecommunications infrastructure.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work is highly relevant to quantum optics and quantum information due to its implementation of multi-user entanglement-based communication and the development of scalable, hardware-compatible quantum network protocols.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Scaling continuous-variable quantum key distribution (CV-QKD) from point-to-point links to multi-user access networks while addressing finite-size security and protocol adaptability.

**Main result.** Experimental demonstration of an active 1:4 CV quantum network achieving a total secret key rate of 1.9e-1 bits/channel use, with a framework that allows for different security/trust levels.

**Method.** A unified Gaussian security framework using a chain-rule decomposition to assign joint key contributions to individual users, combined with DSP-based phase recovery and error correction.

**Model / system.** An active 1:4 multi-user continuous-variable quantum network using a passive optical network (PON) topology with a 1:4 beam splitter, 11 km fiber channels, and coherent state modulation.

**Key observables.** Secret key rate (per-user and total), mutual information, Holevo information, and channel excess noise.

**Important parameters / regimes.** 1.25e9 coherent states exchanged, 125 MBaud symbol rate, modulation variance V_M = 5 SNU, reconciliation efficiency beta = 0.95, and 11 km channel length.

**Assumptions / limitations.** Gaussian attacks (collective attacks), finite-size data block limitations, and varying trust assumptions (trusted, collaborative, or untrusted users).

**Figures summary.** Figure 1a illustrates the 1:4 network topology and the different protocol modes; Figure 3 shows finite-size secret key rates versus the number of signals for the three trust scenarios.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the multi-user CV-QKD problem, describes the experimental setup and hardware, presents the security framework and key rate decomposition, details the experimental results across different trust modes, and concludes with a performance comparison against existing networks.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

In recent years, continuous-variable quantum key distribution (CV-QKD) has become a promising paradigm for enabling secure communication among multiple end users sharing the same telecommunication backbone. CV-QKD with reverse reconciliation naturally enables scalability from conventional point-to-point links to quantum access networks based on passive quantum broadcasting channels. Here, we report an experimental demonstration on an active $1:4$ multi-user CV quantum network (QN) in the finite-size regime. With $1.25\cdot10^9$ coherent states exchanged on each $11\text{km}$ quantum channel, the highest performance for secret key generation totaling $1.9\cdot10^{-1}$ bits/channel use. Furthermore, we investigate adaptable CV-QN protocols that comprehensively allow network operation in various security and key rates requirements of individual users. The results establish the practical security of CV-QN compatible with existing telecommunication for broad deployment, and allowing additional degree of freedom for connected end users in existing infrastructures.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27761"></a>
### [Macroscopic photon counting beating the Poisson noise limit](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27761v1)

**Authors:** Timon Schapeler, Fabian Schlue, Isabell Mischke, Michael Stefszky, Benjamin Brecht, Christine Silberhorn, Tim J. Bartley  
**Type:** experiment · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27761v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `QC/QI experiment` **4/5** · 🔥 `quantum measurements` **4/5** · 🔥 `quantum optics experiment` **4/5**

**Summary.** The researchers developed a method to count large numbers of photons (up to 9000) with precision that exceeds the standard Poisson noise limit. By multiplexing superconducting nanowire detectors, they created a device that functions as a high-sensitivity optical power meter, useful for both quantum state characterization and precision metrology.

**Why it may be interesting.** This is highly relevant for quantum optics and precision metrology as it bridges the gap between single-photon detection and high-sensitivity optical power meters, providing a tool for characterizing large quantum states.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The challenge of achieving precise photon-number resolution for high photon fluxes, specifically overcoming the Poisson noise limit in macroscopic photon counting.

**Main result.** Demonstration of precise photon counting from 0 to over 9000 photons, beating the Poisson noise limit by at least 4.1 dB and achieving sub-single-photon precision up to 276 photons per pulse.

**Method.** Multiplexing eight superconducting nanowire single-photon detectors across 128 temporal modes and using model-informed characterization of 1024 detection bins alongside quantum detector tomography.

**Model / system.** An experimental setup consisting of eight intrinsically photon-number-resolving superconducting nanowire single-photon detectors (SNSPDs) multiplexed into 1024 temporal detection bins.

**Key observables.** Photon number counts, Poisson noise limit, and Positive Operator Valued Measures (POVMs).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Photon range (0 to 9000+), noise reduction (4.1 dB), repetition rate (80 kHz), and optical power (71 pW).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The accuracy relies on the model-informed characterization of the 1024 detection bins.

**Paper structure.** The paper presents an experimental demonstration of a high-capacity photon-counting device, detailing the multiplexing architecture, the characterization of detection bins, the reconstruction of POVMs via tomography, and the performance metrics regarding noise reduction and power sensitivity.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Photon counting is a cornerstone of quantum optics. Here, we demonstrate precisely counting from 0 to over 9000 photons, beating the Poisson noise limit by at least $4.1~\mathrm{dB}$ across this range. We achieve sub-single-photon precision up to 276 photons per pulse. To do so, we multiplex eight intrinsically photon-number-resolving superconducting nanowire single-photon detectors across 128 temporal modes. We use a model-informed characterization of each of the 1024 detection bins, for optimal precision. We perform quantum detector tomography to reconstruct the positive operator valued measures (POVMs) of the complete device, which consists of $1.38\cdot10^8$ matrix elements. At the repetition rate of our experiment of $80~\mathrm{kHz}$, we can precisely count photons corresponding to an optical power of approximately $71~\mathrm{pW}$, bridging the gap from single-photon measurements to high-sensitivity optical power meters. A photon-number-resolving detector of this size, and the tools used to analyze it, will become increasingly important to characterize large quantum states, as well as tasks in precision metrology and optical power standards.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27668"></a>
### [Observation of attractor transitions in active magnon-polaritons under microwatt drives](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27668v1)

**Authors:** Hao Wu, Qichun Liu, Yuanbin Fan, Yulong Liu, Qing Zhao  
**Type:** both · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27668v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `spintronics-quantum-optics interface` **4/5** · `driven-dissipative phase transition` **3/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **3/5** · `quantum optics experiment` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<sub>FIG. 5. Power-dependent stability phase diagram of the active MP revealing its power efﬁciency in achieving nonlinear attractor transitions. a, Dependence of the critical detuning in real time ∆m = ∆0m −Ωmeasured at different driving powers (left panel). **Summary.** This paper reports the first experimental observation of complex attractor transitions, including chaos and frequency combs, in an active magnon-polariton system driven by microwatt powers. By using a self-oscillating cavity, the researchers achieved nonlinear control at power levels four orders of magnitude lower than previous passive systems. This work opens new avenues for low-power nonlinear microwave signal generation and neuromorphic computing.

**Why it may be interesting.** It demonstrates a highly controllable, low-power platform for studying driven-dissipative nonlinear dynamics, period-doubling, and chaos, which are central themes in open quantum systems and nonlinear cavity QED.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The difficulty of experimentally observing and controlling transitions between distinct nonlinear attractors (such as chaos and frequency combs) in conventional passive magnon-polariton systems, which typically require high-power milliwatt-class drives.

**Main result.** The observation of a full route to chaos and the 'explosive growth of bistability' in an active magnon-polariton system using extremely low microwatt-level microwave drives.

**Method.** The researchers used a self-oscillating microwave cavity coupled to a YIG sphere, employing stability analysis of fixed points and numerical simulations of a van der Pol oscillator model to characterize nonlinear dynamics.

**Model / system.** An active magnon-polariton platform consisting of a 1-mm YIG sphere coupled to a microstrip-line cavity with a BJT-based gain element, modeled as a van der Pol oscillator with Kerr nonlinearity and Suhl-mediated scattering.

**Key observables.** Intra-cavity photon number, frequency spectra (limit cycles, fractals, frequency combs, and broadband chaos), and spectral shifts.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Microwatt-level driving power (-35 to -10 dBm), spin-photon coupling strength (g/2pi = 25 MHz), and effective nonlinearity (K/2pi = 3.2 uHz).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The system is modeled using a semiclassical mean-field level approach.

**Figures summary.** Fig 1 compares active vs. passive models and shows simulated phase diagrams; Fig 2 shows the experimental setup and linear dependence; Fig 4 displays experimental frequency offsets, spectral zooms (fractals/chaos), and magnetic-field-dependent Rabi splittings; Fig 5 shows power-dependent stability phase diagrams.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the active vs. passive MP models, describes the experimental setup and BJT-driven architecture, presents stability analysis and phase diagrams, details the experimental observation of power-dependent attractor transitions (from bistability to chaos), and concludes with potential applications in sensing and computing.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Magnon-polaritons provide a room-temperature platform for investigating nonlinear cavity quantum electrodynamics in the microwave domain, but experimentally observing controlled transitions among distinct nonlinear attractors remains challenging in conventional passive systems, where strong external driving is usually required. Here we report the observation of attractor transitions in an active magnon-polariton formed by a self-oscillating microwave cavity coupled to a yttrium iron garne (YIG) sphere. The feedback loop supplies an internal microwave drive, while Kerr frequency pulling and Suhl-mediated magnon-magnon scattering produce an enhanced effective nonlinearity. Stability analysis using experimentally calibrated parameters reveals a rich fixed-point (FP) landscape with multiple unstable-FP phases and a triple-point region. By tuning gain across these phases, we observe the first experimental evidence of explosive growth of bistability, followed by transitions to multifrequency limit cycles, comb-like/fractal spectra, and broadband chaotic dynamics at microwatt powers. Near a critical point, magnetic-field-triggered switching between nonlinear emission states produces spectral shifts up to 162 times the bare gyromagnetic response. By enabling low-power attractor transitions and attractor-switching-amplified spectral response, active magnon-polaritons open opportunities for nonlinear microwave signal generation, high-precision sensing, and neuromorphic computing.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27328"></a>
### [Semiclassical Ehrenfest paths in open quantum systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27328v1)

**Authors:** Xiao-Kan Guo  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27328v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `Keldysh / 2PI / non-Gaussian methods` **4/5** · 🔥 `methods for driven-dissipative` **4/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5** · `quantum measurements` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2604.27328_figures/2604.27328_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 1: The position variance ⟨ˆx2⟩(t) = x(t)2 + σxx(t) for three cases: The quantum case with Dab = diag(2ℏλ, 0) (blue dotted line); the classical case with D = 0 (grey dotted line); the analytical quantum solution (red line). The choices of parameters are specified in the main text.</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper develops a phase-space framework to describe semiclassical Ehrenfest trajectories in open quantum systems using a Gaussian mixture representation. It successfully demonstrates how the evolution of quantum expectation values can be split into coherent motion and irreversible diffusion. This provides a clear physical picture of how environmental effects like dissipation and decoherence lead to the emergence of classical-like trajectories.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a transparent microscopic mechanism for the emergence of classicality from open quantum dynamics, specifically by decomposing the evolution of observables into unitary and dissipative components, which is central to understanding decoherence.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Extending semiclassical Ehrenfest trajectories from closed to open quantum systems and providing a phase-space interpretation of how classical trajectories emerge from open quantum dynamics.

**Main result.** The derivation of a Fokker-Planck equation for a Gaussian mixture representation that allows for the microscopic separation of coherent and irreversible (diffusive) contributions to the evolution of expectation values.

**Method.** The study uses a Gaussian mixture representation of the density matrix, a Local Harmonic Approximation, and a Lagrangian description via a Fokker-Planck equation, validated by Monte-Carlo simulations using Ito stochastic differential equations.

**Model / system.** Open quantum systems governed by the Lindblad master equation, with a specific validation model consisting of a 1D free particle subject to momentum diffusion via a Lindblad operator.

**Key observables.** Expectation values of observables (via Weyl symbols), canonical operators (position and momentum), position variance, and thermodynamic quantities like reversible work and heat.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Centroid (position and momentum), covariance matrix, diffusion matrix, friction vector, coupling strength (lambda), and the 'not-too-squeezed' (NTS) condition.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The Local Harmonic Approximation is used, which assumes the dynamics can be truncated to second order in Weyl symbols and that Gaussian states do not become excessively squeezed.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 compares the evolution of position variance over time for the quantum case (showing growth from dispersion and diffusion), a classical comparison, and the exact analytical solution.

**Paper structure.** The paper first derives the Fokker-Planck equation for the mixing measure of a Gaussian mixture, then embeds a generalized Ehrenfest theorem into this phase-space picture to separate coherent and irreversible dynamics, and finally validates the framework using a 1D free particle model with momentum diffusion.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We study the semiclassical Ehrenfest trajectories in open quantum systems. We first derive in explicit form the Fokker-Planck equation that governs the time evolution of the mixing measure for a Gaussian mixture. Then, we embed the generalized Ehrenfest theorem recently obtained for open quantum systems into this phase-space picture to study the time evolution of the expectations of observable with respect to the Gaussian mixture. We show how the coherent and irreversible contributions are microscopically separated. Our work provides a transparent phase-space interpretation of the emergence of classical trajectories in open quantum dynamics.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.28155"></a>
### [Optimal current-based sensing of phonon temperature using a finite reservoir](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.28155v1)

**Authors:** Sindre Brattegard, Stephanie Matern, Mark T. Mitchison, Saulo V. Moreira  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.28155v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `quantum measurements` **4/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **3/5** · `Kondo & dissipative impurity` **2/5** · `methods for driven-dissipative` **2/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2604.28155_figures/2604.28155_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 1. Sketch of the finite-size reservoir at stationary tem- perature and chemical potential, T and µ, coupled to a phonon bath at temperature Tph and to the quantum dot sys- tem. The finite reservoir is also coupled to the left infinite-size reservoir at temperature TL and µL, while the quantum dot is coupled to another infinite-size reservoir to its right, at tem- perature TR and chemical potential µR.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2604.28155_figures/2604.28155_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 2. Sensitivity rate of the three thermometry schemes as a function of: (left column) phonon temperature and (right column) bias voltage. The top row has electron-phonon cou- pling with an exponent n = 5, while the bottom row has n = 3. The parameters used are TL = TR = 10Γ, Vb = 40Γ, σ = 300Γ/TL, and Vg = −10Γ. When n = 5, we use Σ = 1000σ/T 3 L, and when n = 3, we use Σ = 100σ/TL. In the right column, we set the phonon temperature to Tph = 8Γ.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2604.28155_figures/2604.28155_fig3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 3. Optimised sensitivity rate over gate voltage as the phonon temperature Tph is varied. The inset shows the cor- responding optimal bias voltage. The parameters used are n = 5, TL = TR = 10Γ, Vb = 40Γ, σ = 300Γ/TL, and Σ = 1000σ/T 3 L. For these parameters, we have that ζ = 300, and ξ ≫1, provided the phonon temperature is sufficiently large, i.e., Tph ≳TL/3.</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper investigates how the finite heat capacity of electronic reservoirs can be used to optimize the sensing of phonon temperatures. It compares different current-based measurement strategies and demonstrates that monitoring individual electron jumps provides the highest precision. The results offer a guide for maximizing thermometric sensitivity via gate voltage tuning in nanoscale devices.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a rigorous framework for parameter estimation in non-equilibrium open quantum systems, specifically showing how the thermodynamic properties of a finite environment can be leveraged for high-precision sensing.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Developing high-precision thermometry for phonon temperatures in nanoscale transport setups by exploiting the heat exchange between phonon baths and finite-capacity electronic reservoirs.

**Main result.** The study identifies that monitoring individual electron jumps (Strategy I) achieves optimal precision for phonon temperature sensing and provides an optimization analysis for tuning gate voltage to maximize sensitivity.

**Method.** The authors combine current metrology techniques with a thermodynamic framework for finite reservoirs, using Fisher information and the Cramér-Rao bound to evaluate different measurement strategies.

**Model / system.** A quantum dot coupled to a finite-size electronic reservoir, which is in turn coupled to a phonon bath and an infinite electronic reservoir, described by a master equation in the weak coupling regime.

**Key observables.** Electron tunneling jumps, net particle current (DC current), and quantum dot occupation.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Phonon temperature (Tph), electron-phonon coupling strength (xi), reservoir-to-infinite-reservoir coupling (zeta), and gate voltage (Vg).

**Assumptions / limitations.** Weak coupling regime (Gamma << T), large but finite reservoir, fast internal thermalization (quasiequilibrium), and energy-independent transmission.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the experimental setup schematic; Figure 2 compares sensitivity rates for different strategies as a function of temperature and bias voltage; Figure 3 shows the maximized sensitivity rate optimized over gate voltage.

**Paper structure.** The paper establishes transport and steady-state properties in finite reservoirs, derives the analytical foundations for temperature and chemical potential shifts, applies estimation theory to evaluate measurement strategies, and concludes with an optimization analysis of gate voltage.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

In realistic nanoscale transport set-ups, electron-phonon coupling leads to the exchange of heat between phonon baths and electronic reservoirs with finite heat capacities. Such exchange affects the finite reservoir's temperature. However, this sensitivity of the finite reservoir temperature to the exchange of heat with the finite reservoir has remained unexplored for thermometry. Here, we fill this gap by combining current metrology techniques with a thermodynamic framework encompassing finite reservoirs. We focus on an experimentally realizable set-up with a quantum dot coupled to a finite reservoir and consider two distinct current-based strategies in the long time limit, namely monitoring quanta exchanged between the quantum dot and finite reservoir and the measurement of the total current flowing from the quantum dot into an infinite reservoir. A third strategy involves measurements of the quantum dot occupation. For a large but finite reservoir, we show that the Fisher information for all three strategies captures the finite reservoir's contribution to sensitivity through common factors. We also demonstrate that monitoring quanta exchanged between the system and finite reservoir in the long time limit achieves optimal precision. Finally, we provide an optimization analysis that explores how maximal precision can be achieved within each of the current-based strategies by tuning the gate voltage.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27299"></a>
### [High-Rate Free-Space Continuous-Variable QKD with Self-Referenced Passive State Preparation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27299v1)

**Authors:** H. W. Yin, X. J. Liao, Y. H. Xu, P. Huang, K. T. Zhu, T. Wang, G. H. Zeng  
**Type:** both · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27299v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `QC/QI experiment` **4/5** · 🔥 `quantum optics experiment` **4/5** · `quantum measurements` **2/5**

**Summary.** The researchers developed a new CVQKD method using a self-referenced local local oscillator to overcome noise and instability in free-space communication. They achieved a record-breaking 10.34 Mbps key rate even under significant channel loss. This provides a scalable and practical pathway for high-speed quantum secure communication in real-world environments.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work is highly relevant to quantum optics and quantum networks as it addresses fundamental challenges in maintaining coherence and stability in high-rate, long-distance quantum communication links.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Existing continuous-variable quantum key distribution (CVQKD) schemes using transmitted local oscillators suffer from high photon leakage noise and instability, limiting performance in high-loss free-space channels.

**Main result.** The authors implemented a self-referenced local local oscillator (SR-LLO) CVQKD system that achieves a record-high asymptotic secret key rate of 10.34 Mbps over a free-space channel with up to 23.5 dB loss.

**Method.** The work uses a self-referenced passive state preparation (PSP) scheme combined with a novel pilot scheme for high-precision time-varying frequency and phase compensation, supported by a theoretical proof using temporal-mode theory.

**Model / system.** A continuous-variable quantum key distribution system operating over a free-space channel subject to atmospheric turbulence and high loss.

**Key observables.** Asymptotic secret key rate, excess noise, and signal-to-noise ratio (SNR).

**Important parameters / regimes.** 23.5 dB channel loss, 10.34 Mbps secret key rate.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of noise in transmitted LO schemes, proposes a self-referenced LLO-CVQKD architecture, provides a theoretical equivalence proof using temporal-mode theory, and demonstrates experimental performance in free-space turbulence.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Continuous-variable quantum key distribution (CVQKD) using passive state preparation (PSP) offers low-cost, high-rate secure communication. However, the existing PSP-CVQKD scheme with a transmitted local oscillator has high photon leakage noise and poor stability, making it unsuitable for high-loss transmission. In this work, for the first time, we propose and implement a local local oscillator (LLO) CVQKD system using a self-referenced (SR) PSP scheme, and give a theoretical proof of the equivalence of the PSP and GMCS protocol using temporal-mode theory. By employing the novel self-referenced pilot scheme to achieve high-precision time-varying frequency and phase compensation algorithms, we significantly improve the system' s signal-to-noise ratio and stability. The system achieves a record-high asymptotic secret key rate of 10.34 Mbps over a free-space channel with up to 23.5 dB loss, while maintaining low excess noise and robust performance under turbulent conditions. This work establishes the feasibility of SR-LLO CVQKD, providing a practical pathway toward secure, high-rate quantum communication in realistic environments.

</details>

### [Observation antibunching with classical light in a linear interferometer](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27494v1)

**Authors:** Yu Gu, Yuhan Ma, Yiqi Song, Meixue Chen, Hui Chen, Huaibin Zheng, Yuchen He, Yu Zhou, Fuli Li, Zhuo Xu, Jianbin Liu  
**Type:** both · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27494v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** 🔥 `quantum optics experiment` **4/5** · `interference shaping light` **3/5** · `quantum measurements` **3/5**

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2604.27494_figures/2604.27494_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>
