**Summary.** This paper identifies a new class of discontinuous BBP transitions in random matrices where signal detection occurs via an abrupt jump in overlap. It reveals that finite-size effects can actually lower the detection threshold, allowing signals to be recovered even below the theoretical asymptotic limit.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper investigates the conditions under which the Baik-Ben Arous-Péché (BBP) transition, which governs the detection of low-rank structures in noisy data, becomes discontinuous rather than continuous.

**Main result.** The authors establish that a discontinuous BBP transition occurs when the eigenvalue density vanishes faster than linearly at the spectral edge (exponent a > 2), leading to an abrupt jump in eigenvector overlap and a finite-size 'pre-critical' region for signal recovery.

**Method.** The study employs the resolvent formalism, Stieltjes transform analysis, and free probability theory to analyze the spectral properties of large random matrices.

**Model / system.** The research focuses on spiked random matrix models, specifically deformed Gaussian Orthogonal Ensembles (GOE) with diagonal disorder and reweighted Wishart ensembles.

**Key observables.** Eigenvalue density, eigenvector overlap (correlation between the leading eigenvector and the signal), and the outlier eigenvalue position.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Spike strength (alpha), spectral edge power-law exponent (a), matrix size (N), and the ratio of dimensions (q).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis assumes the continuous spectrum occupies a single interval and focuses on the behavior at the spectral edge in the large-N limit.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 compares continuous vs. discontinuous BBP transitions via the inverse resolvent and overlap; Figure 2 shows the z(x) curve for deformed GOE; Figure 4 demonstrates finite-size scaling of the maximum eigenvalue.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the BBP transition, defines the condition for discontinuity via spectral density decay, analyzes specific ensembles (deformed GOE and Wishart), develops a finite-size scaling theory, and discusses implications for machine learning and biological systems.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

The Baik-Ben Arous-Peche (BBP) transition sets fundamental limits for detecting low-rank structure in noisy high-dimensional data and underlies a wide range of spectral methods in many fields from physics to statistics and data sciences. In standard settings, this transition is continuous, implying that signal recovery emerges gradually above a sharp threshold. We show that BBP transitions can instead be discontinuous in very general settings and provide a full theory of this phenomenon. When the eigenvalue density vanishes faster than linearly at the spectral edge, the overlap between the leading eigenvector and the signal jumps discontinuously at the critical point. We study this mechanism in deformed Gaussian and reweighted Wishart ensembles. We analyze in detail the finite-size effects, which play a central and qualitatively new role in the discontinuous BBP transition. Unlike the continuous BBP transition, we establish the existence of an extended pre-critical region where informative eigenvectors emerge well before the asymptotic threshold. The main consequence-and difference from the continuous BBP transition-is that signal recovery can occur at significantly lower signal-to-noise ratio and it is accompanied by strong sample-to-sample variability. Our results show the relevance and the novelty of the discontinuous BBP transition, and highlight the practical implications for signal detection.

</details>

### [Exotic Spin Excitation Continuum in a Weakly Coupled Quantum Chainsaw Antiferromagnet](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27310v1)

**Summary.** The researchers investigated a Ti-based kagome-related antiferromagnet and discovered that structural distortions create a network of weakly coupled spin chains. This leads to an exotic excitation continuum and rod-like scattering, demonstrating that 1D-like fractionalization can exist within a 2D lattice structure.

**Why it may be interesting.** The discovery of a mechanism where 1D-like fractionalized excitations persist within a 2D lattice provides new insights into many-body dynamics and the stability of quantum-disordered states across dimensional crossovers.

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Understanding the dimensional crossover of quantum disorder and how fractionalized excitations evolve when transitioning from 1D criticality to 2D topological order.

**Main result.** The study identifies a regime of 'anisotropic fractionalization' in a Ti-based kagome-related antiferromagnet, where 1D-like signatures persist in a 2D lattice due to structural distortions.

**Method.** Inelastic neutron scattering (INS) and neutron diffraction were performed on a single crystal at the Spallation Neutron Source, complemented by crystal structure refinement and Linear Spin Wave theory.

**Model / system.** The system is Cs8LiNa3Ti12F48, a Ti-based quantum antiferromagnet featuring a frustrated network of weakly coupled spin-1/2 'chainsaws' within distorted kagome planes.

**Key observables.** Dynamic spin correlation function S(Q, h-omega), equal-time response function S(Q), magnetic susceptibility, and crystal structure parameters.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Curie-Weiss temperature Theta_CW = -36.9 K, exchange couplings ranging from J_D = 1.22 meV to J_A = 11.26 meV, and an excitation continuum extending up to ~11 meV.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The use of Linear Spin Wave theory as a minimal effective Hamiltonian to describe the dispersion, despite its failure to capture the continuum.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of dimensional crossover, describes the crystal structure and magnetic properties of the Ti-based material, presents neutron scattering data showing the excitation continuum and rod-like scattering, and concludes by discussing the principle of anisotropic fractionalization.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Collective motions in strongly interacting magnets involve many spins and are often described in terms of integer-spin excitations. However, in certain cases, the collective motion can behave as if these integer excitations break apart into smaller, particle-like entities with unusual properties. Such fractionalized excitations in quantum magnets are commonly associated either with topological order in two dimensions or with criticality in one dimension. It remains unclear how these distinct mechanisms are connected across a dimensional crossover. Here we investigate the Ti-based quantum antiferromagnet, $Cs_{8}LiNa_{3}Ti_{12}F_{48}$, in which $Ti^{3+}$ ($3d^{1}$, $S=1/2$) ions interact antiferromagnetically within distorted kagome planes. Our inelastic neutron scattering study on a single crystal reveals a frustrated network of weakly coupled spin-$1/2$ chainsaws, realizing a regime of dimensional frustration in which interchain couplings fail to establish coherent two-dimensional order. The magnetic excitation spectrum exhibits a strong continuum spanning the full measured momentum and energy phase space. In addition, the dynamic spin correlation function displays rod-like scattering in momentum space, indicating a quasi-one-dimensional nature of the magnetic correlations. These results point to fractionalized excitations with intrinsically directional character, demonstrating that signatures of one-dimensional criticality can persist within a two-dimensional lattice. Our findings establish anisotropic fractionalization as a distinct organizing principle for quantum-disordered states.

</details>

### [Finite Imaginary-Time Evolution for Polynomial Unconstrained Binary Optimization](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27482v1)

**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27482v1>

**Summary.** This paper introduces FinITE, a method to implement finite imaginary-time evolution for optimization problems on quantum computers using LCU and amplitude amplification. It provides a rigorous mathematical framework to optimize the evolution time and success probability, specifically for higher-order optimization problems without needing complex quadratization.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Implementing non-unitary imaginary-time evolution (ITE) on quantum hardware for solving optimization problems, specifically managing the trade-off between ground-state fidelity and the success probability of the LCU implementation.

**Main result.** The authors derive an exact identity relating LCU success probability and ground-subspace fidelity, and provide a closed-form threshold for the imaginary-time parameter beta to guarantee a target fidelity.

**Method.** The FinITE algorithm uses the Linear-Combination-of-Unitaries (LCU) framework for termwise block-encoding of commuting Pauli-Z strings, combined with Fixed-Point Amplitude Amplification (FPAA) to boost success probability.

**Model / system.** The method targets Polynomial Unconstrained Binary Optimization (PUBO) problems, including QUBO and Higher-order UnCO (HUBO) instances, represented by diagonal Pauli-Z cost Hamiltonians.

**Key observables.** LCU success probability (P_LCU), ground-subspace fidelity (F_g), and the product of success probability and fidelity.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Imaginary time (beta), spectral gap (Delta), initial ground-subspace overlap (gamma_0), and the l1-norm of Pauli coefficients (W).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The Hamiltonian terms must be pairwise-commuting (to avoid Trotter error), and the initial state must have a non-zero overlap with the ground subspace.

**Figures summary.** Simulations verifying the exponential decay identity of the success-fidelity product, a comparison of different initial state overlaps, and a quantum circuit diagram for gate decomposition.

**Paper structure.** Introduction to ITE and PUBO; development of the FinITE LCU construction; mathematical derivation of the success-fidelity identity and beta-threshold rule; complexity analysis of the FPAA-integrated procedure; and numerical validation using statevector and shot-based simulations.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Imaginary-time evolution is a standard primitive for ground-state preparation but is nonunitary, precluding direct quantum implementation. We develop Finite Imaginary-Time Evolution (FinITE), a finite-beta construction for diagonal Pauli-Z cost Hamiltonians arising from polynomial unconstrained binary optimization (PUBO) instances, including QUBO and HUBO cases. FinITE uses the linear-combination-of-unitaries (LCU) framework to implement a scaled imaginary-time propagator. The commuting Pauli-Z structure makes termwise block-encodings compose without product-formula error, and higher-order Pauli-Z terms are handled directly without quadratization. The structure yields an exact finite-beta identity between the LCU success probability and the ground-subspace fidelity. Combined with a gap-based fidelity lower bound, the identity yields a closed-form sufficient imaginary-time threshold beta-star for a chosen target fidelity. The threshold depends on estimates of the spectral gap and the initial ground-subspace overlap. Because the LCU success event is flagged by a known ancilla outcome, we integrate fixed-point amplitude amplification with an explicit query-complexity bound. Statevector simulations verify the identity on a five-vertex MaxCut (QUBO) and an eight-qubit cubic HUBO instance, and shot-based simulations on the MaxCut instance illustrate the predicted finite-beta threshold and amplification procedure.

</details>

### [g-tensor Optimization in Ge/SiGe Quantum Dots](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.28081v1)

**Authors:** Aram Shojaei, Edmondo Valvo, Maximilian Rimbach-Russ, Eliska Greplova, Ana Silva  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.28081v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable

**Summary.** This paper presents a numerical framework to optimize the g-tensor in germanium-based quantum dots by engineering the heterostructure potential. By adjusting silicon concentration, the researchers show it is possible to suppress unwanted g-tensor components, which helps mitigate device variability and enables more reliable qubit operations for scalable quantum computing.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Device performance in planar germanium hole-spin qubit platforms is limited by quantum dot variability, which causes uncertain energy levels and random spin quantization axis orientations.

**Main result.** The authors developed a flexible optimization framework that demonstrates how reshaping the out-of-plane potential via silicon concentration adjustment can suppress in-plane g-tensor components to enable gapless single-spin qubit encoding.

**Method.** A numerical optimization framework designed for engineering g-tensor properties through heterostructure engineering.

**Model / system.** A SiGe-Ge-SiGe quantum well heterostructure hosting hole-spin qubits.

**Key observables.** g-tensor components (specifically in-plane vs. out-of-plane) and the spin quantization axis orientation.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Silicon concentration within the quantum well and the resulting out-of-plane potential profile.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of variability in Ge/SiGe quantum dots, presents a new optimization framework for g-tensor engineering, uses the suppression of in-plane g-tensor components as a benchmark case, and concludes with the implications for scalable quantum computing.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Planar germanium heterostructures hosting hole-spin qubits are among the leading platforms for scalable semiconductor-based quantum computing. Yet, device performance is hindered by significant quantum dot variability, which leads to uncertainty in qubit energy levels and random orientations of the spin quantization axis. Tailored control of the g-tensor offers a strategy to overcome these limitations and achieve more reliable qubit operations. Here, we introduce a flexible optimization framework for engineering g-tensor properties. As a benchmark, we numerically obtain the optimal reshaping of the out-of-plane potential in a SiGe-Ge-SiGe quantum well to suppress the in-plane g-tensor components and realize the recently proposed gapless single-spin qubit encoding. This reshaping is achieved through heterostructure engineering, specifically by adjusting the silicon concentration within the quantum well, though the framework remains readily adaptable to alternative design objectives. Our results provide practical design principles for improving the tunability of the spin response, paving the way towards large-scale germanium-based quantum computers.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27779"></a>
### [Geometric memory in incomplete phase transitions across dimensions](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27779v1)

**Authors:** F. Tolea, M. Tolea  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27779v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

The progressive crowding reduces available perimeter for growth and only small squares can grow towards jamming.</sub>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<sub>Fig. 1 illustrates the gradual filling of a large square domain (side A = 30) with smaller squares whose sizes range from Lmin = 3 to Lmax = 7. In our model, each newly placed square nucleates at the minimum size and then “grows” to a target size drawn randomly from the interval (Lmin, Lmax), while preserving its square shape. Owing to this randomness in size selection, the early stages of the transformation contain comparable numbers of squares of all sizes. Fig. 1a displays a single random placement of the first few squares, but when averaged over many realizations the number of squares per size tends to equalize. Panels (b) and (c) make visually clear how, as space fills, new squares are...</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2604.27779_figures/2604.27779_fig3.jpg" width="500"><br>

Brute-force seeding uniformly among available L3 min places, then growth up to a random maximum intrinsic size, not bigger than Lmax = 7. In three dimensions, accessible free surface collapses faster than in 2D, favoring earlier lack of space for larger cubes.</sub>

</details>

<img src="2604.27779_figures/2604.27779_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>

**Summary.** This paper demonstrates that memory effects in phase transitions can emerge purely from geometric constraints like nucleation, growth, and impingement without needing explicit thermodynamics. It shows that the strength of this 'geometric memory' is highly dependent on the dimensionality of the system, being most pronounced in 2D.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating the mechanism of geometric memory in incomplete first-order solid-state phase transitions and how dimensionality (2D, 3D, and 3D lamellar) affects the strength of this memory effect.

**Main result.** The study finds that memory is robust across all geometries but is strongest in 2D and weakest in 3D lamellar structures, driven purely by geometric constraints like growth and impingement.

**Method.** A discrete lattice-based stochastic nucleation-and-growth model using brute-force seeding and shape-preserving dilation algorithms.

**Model / system.** A minimal geometric model of phase transformations involving the nucleation and self-similar growth of plates (2D squares), cubes (3D), and lamellae (3D with fixed thickness) that are arrested by impingement or intrinsic size limits.

**Key observables.** Size Mass Ratio (SMR), Shannon size-entropy, plate-size distributions, and simulated Differential Scanning Calorimetry (DSC) signals.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Minimum and maximum plate sizes (Lmin, Lmax), domain size (A), lamellar thickness (Tw), and the arrest size (s).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The model excludes explicit energetic, elastic, or thermodynamic terms, relying solely on geometric blocking; it also assumes the reverse transformation proceeds via the preferential disappearance of smaller plates.

**Figures summary.** Snapshots of growth progression and arrest-regrowth cycles; mass-per-size histograms showing depletion at arrested sizes; and simulated DSC signals showing characteristic dips or shoulders.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the geometric memory concept, describes the nucleation-and-growth model, presents results for 2D, 3D, and 3DL geometries, quantifies memory via SMR and entropy, and discusses the implications of dimensionality and the 'hammering' effect.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We model a direct solid-state phase transition through a nucleation-and-growth process in which plates have simple, regular shapes - squares, cubes, or square-faced lamellae - and grow homothetically (self-similarly) until they either reach a randomly assigned maximum size or are stopped by impingement with previously formed plates. The reverse transformation is represented by the preferential disappearance of smaller plates, while larger plates are retained during an incomplete reversion. A subsequent direct transformation therefore produces a modified plate-size distribution, a memory effect that forms the main focus of this study. Building upon an earlier two-dimensional (2D) formulation, we extend the model to cubes (3D) and to lamellar plates (3DL) in order to examine how dimensionality affects transformation memory. We introduce a quantitative descriptor of memory, the size mass ratio, and find that memory is robust in all geometries but overall stronger in 2D than in 3D or 3DL. We provide growth snapshots, arrest-regrowth cycles, size distributions, and differential scanning calorimetry simulations, and we compute the Shannon size-entropy to quantify configurational diversity. Although motivated by the thermal memory effect in shape-memory alloys, the model more generally identifies a purely geometric mechanism for memory in first-order solid-solid transformations, highlighting the role of dimensionality and geometric blocking in controlling the strength of transformation memory.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27817"></a>
### [High-Girth Regular Quantum LDPC Codes from Square-Base Hypergraph Products via CPM Lifts](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27817v1)

**Authors:** Koki Okada, Kenta Kasai  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27817v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<sub>Figure 1: p–FER plot for the randomized P = 64 lift derived from the generalized-quadrangle base B15. Each point aggregates independent decoding trials at the same p, using the degeneracy- aware BP decoder followed by OSD-lite post-processing; shaded bands indicate Wilson 95% confidence intervals. Zero-failure points are plotted at the upper endpoint of the Wilson interval. The dashed vertical line is the population-dynamics estimate pDE ≈0.1529 of the BP density- evolution threshold for the (3, 6)-regular CSS-LDPC ensemble on the depolarizing channel, and the dash-dotted vertical line is the depolarizing-channel hashing limit phash ≈0.18929.</sub>

**Summary.** This paper presents a method for constructing large-scale, regular quantum LDPC codes with high girth by lifting small square-base matrices. It demonstrates that these codes can achieve extremely low decoding failure rates under significant depolarizing noise, highlighting the importance of degeneracy in quantum error correction.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Designing regular, high-girth quantum low-density parity-check (QLDPC) codes by controlling short cycles and logical qubit counts during the lifting of square-base hypergraph product constructions.

**Main result.** The authors constructed a (3,6)-regular CSS-LDPC code with parameters [[28800, 62, 8]] that demonstrates zero decoding failures in nearly 300 million trials at a depolarizing probability of 0.1402.

**Method.** The study uses square-base CSS hypergraph product (HGP) constructions combined with Circulant Permutation Matrix (CPM) lifts, utilizing finite-geometric incidence structures and randomized local searches to satisfy CSS orthogonality and girth constraints.

**Model / system.** The study focuses on quantum error-correcting codes, specifically the Calderbank-Shor-Steane (CSS) construction under a depolarizing noise model.

**Key observables.** Tanner girth, decoding failure rate (Frame Error Rate), logical qubit count (k), and the distinction between exact and degenerate decoding success.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Depolarizing probability p = 0.1402, code parameters [[28800, 62, 8]], and the theoretical hashing limit and BP density-evolution threshold.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The construction is limited to a girth of 8 due to orthogonality-forced cycles, and the design quantum rate is zero for the square-base case.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows a performance plot of the Frame Error Rate versus p; Figures 2 and 3 display matrix plots of various square base matrices (B7, B13, B15, etc.); Figure 4 visualizes the resulting HGP check matrices.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the square-base HGP construction, provides algebraic conditions for regularity and girth, analyzes the effect of CPM lifting on cycles and logical qubits, presents specific code constructions using finite geometries, and concludes with numerical decoding performance simulations.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We study square-base Calderbank--Shor--Steane (CSS) hypergraph-product codes as a finite-length class for regular high-girth quantum low-density parity-check (LDPC) design. For base matrices of small column weight, we give checkable conditions for regularity, rank deficiency, and short-cycle exclusion, and we present explicit column-weight-three and column-weight-four examples with Tanner girth 6 and 8. We also analyze circulant permutation matrix (CPM) lifts of this class. Using the standard voltage-sum criterion, we identify orthogonality-forced Tanner 8-cycles and show that CPM lifting cannot raise the Tanner girth beyond 8 when these cycles are present. As a representative finite-length instance, a randomized CPM lift of the girth-8 base construction gives a $[[28800,62]]$ girth-8 $(3,6)$-regular CSS-LDPC code. Under degeneracy-aware belief-propagation decoding with optional ordered-statistics-decoding-lite post-processing, this code produced zero decoding failures in $2.993\times 10^8$ independent trials at depolarizing probability $p=0.1402$; the Wilson 95% upper confidence bound is $1.28\times 10^{-8}$.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27051"></a>
### [Local Current Algebra for the HK Universality Class](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27051v1)

**Authors:** Yuting Bai, Philip W. Phillips  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** strongly correlated electrons · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27051v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2604.27051_figures/2604.27051_page2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 2</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2604.27051_figures/2604.27051_page3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 3</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2604.27051_figures/2604.27051_page4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 4</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2604.27051_figures/2604.27051_page5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 5</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2604.27051_figures/2604.27051_page6.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 6</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper resolves a major criticism of the Hatsugai-Kohmoto model by showing that its apparent non-locality in real space can be eliminated using a local current algebra. By establishing a local correspondence, the authors reinforce the utility of current algebras for describing strong interactions in Mott insulators.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper addresses the non-locality in real space of the Hatsugai-Kohmoto (HK) model, a known criticism of this model for doped Mott insulators.

**Main result.** The authors demonstrate that a Hamiltonian expressed via local real-space currents obeying an su(2) affine Lie algebra eliminates the non-locality, and that the charge susceptibility computed from this current Hamiltonian is identical to the original fermionic formulation.

**Method.** The study uses the Bjorken-Johnson-Low (BJL) prescription to derive equal-time commutation relations from microscopic correlation functions and employs a current algebra formulation (Sugawara-like construction) in the Dirac limit.

**Model / system.** The system is a 1D doped Mott insulator described by the Hatsugai-Kohmoto (HK) model, which is a solvable alternative to the Hubbard model that captures Mott physics via the breaking of Z2 symmetry.

**Key observables.** Charge susceptibility (direct and mixing components), density operators, and current operators.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Interaction strength U, Fermi momentum kF, Fermi velocity vF, and the Dirac limit (kF, m -> infinity).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The dispersion is assumed to be quadratic, and the results are presented in the low-energy, long-wavelength (q -> 0) limit.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by identifying the non-locality problem in the HK model, then introduces the current algebra formulation. It uses the BJL prescription to derive commutators, proves the necessity of multi-component currents, and concludes by verifying that the resulting susceptibility matches the original model.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We show that a Hamiltonian in terms of the local real-space currents obeying an $\mathfrak{su}_1(2)$ affine Lie algebra eliminates the non-locality in the Hatsugai-Kohmoto model for a doped Mott insulator. We establish this local correspondence through the Bjorken-Johnson-Low prescription for anomalous commutators. With this result, we show that the charge susceptibility computed from the current Hamiltonian is identical to that with the elemental Fermionic fields. Consequently, the HK model is local in real space, though not in terms of the Fermionic fields, thereby eliminating the key criticism of this model and reinforcing the utility of current algebras for strong interactions.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.28026"></a>
### [Order by disorder up to arbitrarily high temperature](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.28026v1)

**Authors:** Ravish Mehta  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.28026v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2604.28026_figures/2604.28026_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 1: A configuration with two contours γ1 and γ2 with the boundary Bpωq denoted by the dark grey region and the patterned regions representing boundaries of the contours. The outer boundary has the phase η1 and the interior boundary has the same phase as that of the interior components along which they are drawn.</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper proves that certain classical lattice models exhibit long-range checkerboard order at arbitrarily high temperatures. This phenomenon, known as 'order by disorder,' occurs because thermal fluctuations (entropy) select specific ordered patterns even though they are not the energy-minimizing ground states. The result is established using rigorous mathematical tools like Pirogov-Sinai theory.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Proving the existence of long-range checkerboard order in a class of classical lattice models at arbitrarily high temperatures, where the ordering is driven by entropy rather than energy minimization.

**Main result.** The author proves that for sufficiently small inverse temperature (high temperature), the Gibbs measure is concentrated near checkerboard configurations, establishing the existence of distinct infinite-volume Gibbs states.

**Method.** The proof utilizes Pirogov-Sinai theory, cluster expansion, and a polymer representation of the partition function, supported by a Peierls-type bound on contour surface energy.

**Model / system.** A classical lattice model on a d-dimensional hypercubic lattice (d >= 2) with an unbounded on-site state space (bosonic occupation numbers) and a nearest-neighbor interaction function satisfying specific symmetry and growth conditions.

**Key observables.** The difference between the Gibbs measure of occupation labels and the reference checkerboard configurations; the existence of distinct infinite-volume Gibbs states.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Inverse temperature (beta) in the limit beta -> 0; on-site energy scale (U); growth exponent (alpha).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The proof relies on the validity of the contour weight bound and the existence of a polymer representation within the high-temperature regime.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 illustrates a configuration with two contours, showing the boundary of a macro-site.

**Paper structure.** The paper identifies the model and its interaction conditions, constructs a macro-lattice to define reference configurations, derives a polymer representation of the partition function, establishes Peierls-type bounds on contour energy, and concludes with the proof of phase coexistence and uniform convergence to the checkerboard states.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We prove that a class of classical lattice models on $\mathbb{Z}^d$ ($d \geq 2$) with on-site space $\mathbb{N}_0$ exhibits long-range checkerboard order at sufficiently high temperature. The model has a nearest-neighbour interaction $f : \mathbb{N}_0 \times \mathbb{N}_0 \to [0,\infty)$ satisfying four structural conditions, subsuming the recently introduced power-law model of Han--Huang--Komargodski--Lucas--Popov (arXiv:2503.22789) as a special case. The ordering mechanism is purely entropic: the checkerboard configurations are not energy minimisers, but are selected by the partial trace over occupation numbers in the $β\to 0$ limit. The proof uses Pirogov--Sinai theory and the key input is a Peierls bound.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27522"></a>
### [Pauli equation in spaces of constant curvature and extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27522v1)

**Authors:** Abdaljalel E. Alizzi, Zurab K. Silagadze  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27522v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2604.27522_figures/2604.27522_page2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 2</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2604.27522_figures/2604.27522_page3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 3</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2604.27522_figures/2604.27522_page4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 4</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2604.27522_figures/2604.27522_page5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 5</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2604.27522_figures/2604.27522_page6.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 6</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** The paper critiques the use of the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method for solving Heun-type differential equations in quantum mechanics. It shows that while the method can suggest an energy spectrum for a particle in curved space, the mathematical conditions for the existence of those solutions are actually impossible to satisfy. This highlights a significant pitfall when applying algebraic methods to complex potentials in non-Euclidean geometries.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper investigates the validity of using the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov (ENU) method to find analytical solutions for the Pauli equation in spaces of constant curvature.

**Main result.** The authors demonstrate that the ENU method provides only a necessary but not sufficient condition for polynomial solutions in Heun-type equations, leading to a mathematical inconsistency where the required energy spectrum cannot actually exist.

**Method.** The study employs the vierbein formalism, separation of variables using Wigner D-functions, and a matrix determinant analysis to check for the existence of polynomial solutions in the radial Heun equation.

**Model / system.** A spin-1/2 particle (such as an electron) in a Coulomb potential within a space of constant curvature, described by the non-relativistic limit of the Dirac equation (the Pauli equation).

**Key observables.** Energy spectrum (eigenvalues) and the existence of polynomial solutions for the radial wave function.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Curvature (kappa), total angular momentum (j), magnetic quantum number (m), and the non-relativistic regime (epsilon + e^2/T_kappa(r) << m).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The study assumes the use of the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method and examines the non-relativistic limit of the Dirac equation in curved spacetime.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by deriving the radial Pauli equation from the Dirac equation in curved space, applies the extended NU method to find a potential energy spectrum, and then uses a tridiagonal matrix analysis to prove the mathematical invalidity of the derived solutions.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We apply the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method to the non-relativistic limit of the Dirac equation with a Coulomb potential in spaces of constant curvature. In this case, the radial equation reduces to the Heun equation, and the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method easily yields a quantization condition which leads to necessary condition under which the resulting Heun equation can have polynomial solutions. The energy spectrum implied by the quantization condition is virtually identical to the spectrum of a spinless particle obtained using the Schrödinger equation, except for the absence of the ``geometric potential", confirming the non-commutativity of the naive non-relativistic limit with the ``squaring" of the Dirac equation, first discovered on curved surfaces. However, the necessary conditions for the existence of polynomial solutions cannot be met, and this fact undermines the reliability of the results obtained. This circumstance forces us to conclude that the extended Nikiforov-Uvarov method has limited, if any, value when considering similar problems in quantum mechanics.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27324"></a>
### [Q3SAT-GPT: A Generative Model for Discovering Quantum Circuits for the 3-SAT Problem](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27324v1)

**Authors:** Pratim Ugale, Ilya Tyagin, Karunya Shirali, Kien X. Nguyen, Ilya Safro  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27324v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2604.27324_figures/2604.27324_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Fig. 1: A Representative Conflict Illustration. Operator gener- ators ˆAi are labeled with their corresponding gradient mag- nitudes in parentheses. In (a), selecting the highest individual gradient ( ˆA1) blocks the selection possibility of ˆA4 and ˆA5, leading to a lower total sum of gradients as compared to (b).</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2604.27324_figures/2604.27324_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Fig. 2: Incompatibility graph representation for a 3-qubit problem instance, used for operator selection. Each node in the graph represents a candidate unitary operator from the pool P, An edge connects two nodes if and only if their corresponding operators have overlapping qubit support. Sets of overlapping two-qubit operators form fully connected cliques and are omitted to maintain legibility.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2604.27324_figures/2604.27324_fig3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Fig. 3: Detailed pipeline demonstrating formatting, tokenization, and embeddings. The | delimiter is used to segment clauses, with explicit OR (∨) tokens omitted.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2604.27324_figures/2604.27324_fig4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Fig. 4: Comparison of the energy convergence across adap- tations. Note that in Figure (b), plots of TETRIS-QAOA and ADAPT-QAOA overlap due to the same operators being chosen by both the methods (see Figure 6).</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2604.27324_figures/2604.27324_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Fig. 5: Comparison of the maximum gradient norm across all operators in the mixer pool. Note that in Figure (b), plots of TETRIS-QAOA and ADAPT-QAOA overlap due to the same operators having the maximum gradient for the most part (see Figure 6).</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper introduces Q3SAT-GPT, a generative AI model that learns to design quantum circuits for solving 3-SAT problems. By training on circuits generated by a novel adaptive method (MosaicADAPT-QAOA), the model can bypass expensive classical optimization during inference, providing a scalable route for quantum algorithm discovery.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The high computational cost and complexity of discovering optimized quantum circuits for the Max-E3-SAT combinatorial optimization problem using traditional adaptive QAOA methods.

**Main result.** The Q3SAT-GPT generative model can predict high-quality quantum circuits in a single forward pass, achieving significant speedups in amortized inference time while maintaining strong solution quality.

**Method.** A transformer-based generative architecture (Q3SAT-GPT) is trained on high-quality circuit trajectories produced by a new adaptive strategy called MosaicADAPT-QAOA, which uses a Maximum Weight Independent Set approach to select disjoint operators.

**Model / system.** The study focuses on the Max-E3-SAT problem, mapping classical 3-CNF formulas to a cost Hamiltonian using a Higher-Order Unconstrained Binary Optimization (HUBO) formulation with Pauli-Z operators.

**Key observables.** Approximation Ratio (AR), Error Rate (ER) of circuit validity, and amortized inference time.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Phase transition ratio (alpha = m/n), circuit depth, and initial variational angles (gamma_0, beta_0).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The model's performance is limited by the quality of the training data from MosaicADAPT-QAOA, and it assumes the 3-SAT instances can be effectively represented via Literal-Clause Graph (LCG) embeddings.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the failure of greedy operator selection; Figure 2 depicts an incompatibility graph; Figure 3 illustrates the transformer pipeline and embeddings; Figure 4 shows energy convergence; Figure 7 compares predicted vs. optimized variational parameters.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of circuit discovery, presents the MosaicADAPT-QAOA adaptive strategy, details the Q3SAT-GPT generative architecture and training pipeline, evaluates performance on random and balanced 3-SAT instances, and discusses scalability and limitations.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

This work introduces Q3SAT-GPT, a generative model for discovering quantum circuits for the Max-E3-SAT problem. Our method learns from high-performing QAOA-style ansätze to directly generate candidate circuits. To create high-quality supervision, we also introduce Mosaic Adaptive QAOA (MosaicADAPT-QAOA), an adaptive strategy for constructing low-depth QAOA circuits by selecting subsets of mixer operators in each step, rather than inserting operators sequentially. The resulting circuits serve as training data for the generative model, allowing it to learn effective circuit design patterns while eliminating the need for costly variational optimization at inference time. Experiments show that our framework attains strong solution quality with shallow circuits and scales significantly better than both our adaptive construction procedure and conventional variational baselines. Our results establish generative modeling as a high-performance route toward the scalable discovery of quantum optimization circuits, demonstrating that these models can effectively internalize circuit logic while providing a foundation for future, instance-aware inductive biases. Reproducibility: The source code is available at https://github.com/pratimugale/Q3SAT-GPT.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27632"></a>
### [Quantum Scalar Spin Chirality in Coplanar Kagome Antiferromagnets](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27632v1)

**Authors:** Nanse Esaki, Gyungchoon Go, Se Kwon Kim  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** strongly correlated electrons · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27632v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable

**Summary.** This paper shows that even in magnets where spins are arranged in a plane, quantum fluctuations can create a sense of 'handedness' or scalar spin chirality. This effect is significant because it can be as strong as the chirality found in more complex noncoplanar magnetic structures.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating whether quantum fluctuations can generate scalar spin chirality in antiferromagnets that possess coplanar ground-state spin configurations.

**Main result.** The authors demonstrate that quantum fluctuations can induce scalar spin chirality at zero temperature in coplanar kagome antiferromagnets, provided certain symmetry-breaking conditions are met. These fluctuations can grow with temperature and reach magnitudes comparable to the static chirality found in noncoplanar systems.

**Method.** Theoretical analysis of quantum fluctuations and the effective Hamiltonian describing fluctuations in a kagome antiferromagnet.

**Model / system.** A kagome antiferromagnet with coplanar ordered ground-state spin configurations.

**Key observables.** Scalar spin chirality and its fluctuations.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Zero temperature, temperature-dependent magnon excitations, and the magnetic point group of the classical ground state.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The presence of scalar spin chirality depends on the breaking of an effective time-reversal-like antiunitary symmetry in the fluctuation Hamiltonian.

**Paper structure.** The paper presents a theoretical demonstration of quantum-induced scalar spin chirality, discusses the symmetry requirements for its emergence in coplanar kagome systems, and analyzes the temperature dependence of these fluctuations.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We theoretically demonstrate that quantum fluctuations inherent to antiferromagnets can generate scalar spin chirality at zero temperature even in coplanar ordered magnets. In a kagome antiferromagnet with coplanar ground-state spin configurations, the quantum-fluctuation-induced scalar spin chirality is shown to arise at zero temperature when an effective time-reversal-like antiunitary symmetry is broken in the Hamiltonian describing fluctuations, and a magnetic point group of the classical ground state allows for its presence. The scalar spin chirality fluctuations are shown to grow further with increasing temperature by thermally excited magnons. These scalar spin chirality fluctuations can reach a magnitude comparable to the static one predicted for noncoplanar spin structures, highlighting their physical implications in coplanar spin systems.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27226"></a>
### [Ratio-Dependent Contrarian Activation in Opinion Dynamics](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27226v1)

**Authors:** Serge Galam  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27226v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2604.27226_figures/2604.27226_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 1: The two domains of the landscape of the dynamics induced by the variation of c3,0 and c2,1. The domains are separated by the line c3,0 = 1 3(1 −3c2,1). Inside the colored area, pA,B exist and are attractors with pc being a tipping point. Outside the colored area in the white area only the fixed point pc = 1</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2604.27226_figures/2604.27226_fig2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 2: Various main stages of the variation pA in red and pB in blue as a function of c2,1 for the series of given values c3,0 = 0, 0.01, 0.17, 0.3, 0.35, 0.99. The fixed point pc = 1</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2604.27226_figures/2604.27226_fig3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 3: The complete landscape of the dynamics including alternating regimes. Four domains are shown as a function of c3,0 and c2,1. The domains are separated by the lines c3,0 = 1</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2604.27226_figures/2604.27226_fig4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 4: Four different regimes produced by the update Equation (11) with a tipping point coupled to two attractors, a single attractor, an alternating single attractor and an alternating tipping point coupled to two alternating attractors, for respectively (c3,0 = 0.05, c2,1 = 0.15), (c3,0 = 0.12, c2,1 = 0.22), (c3,0 = 0.88, c2,1 = 0.78), (c3,0 = 0.95, c2,1 = 0.85).</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2604.27226_figures/2604.27226_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Figure 5: Various main stages of the variation p ¯ A in red and p ¯B in blue as a function of c2,1 for the series of given values c3,0 = 0, 0.01, 0.17, 0.3, 0.35, 0.99. The fixed point pc = 1</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper extends the Galam Majority Model by introducing contrarians whose behavior depends on the local ratio of majority to minority. It maps out a complex two-dimensional landscape of opinion dynamics, revealing how different types of non-conformity can either stabilize a majority or drive a system toward a 50/50 random winner.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Investigating how 'mixed contrarians'—whose activation depends on the local majority/minority ratio—impact the evolution and stability of opinions in a heterogeneous population.

**Main result.** The study identifies a two-dimensional landscape of four distinct dynamical domains, including regimes of majority/minority winners, a 50/50 polarized attractor, and alternating regimes.

**Method.** Analytical derivation of an explicit update equation for opinion proportions, followed by fixed-point and stability analysis using Taylor expansion.

**Model / system.** An extension of the Galam Majority Model (GMM) involving discussion groups of size N=3 with two competing opinions and two types of contrarians (c3,0 and c2,1) whose activation depends on the local group configuration.

**Key observables.** Proportion of agents with opinion A (p_n), fixed points (attractors), tipping points, and stability derivative (d3).

**Important parameters / regimes.** c3,0 (contrarian probability in unanimous groups), c2,1 (contrarian probability in 2:1 groups), and group size N=3.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The model assumes a discrete-time update process and a fixed group size of 3 with symmetric behavior between opinions A and B.

**Figures summary.** Figure 5 shows the variation of final opinion proportions as a function of c2,1 for different c3,0 values, highlighting the transition between different dynamical attractors.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the problem of ratio-dependent contrarians, defines the extended Galam Majority Model, derives the analytical update equation and fixed points, performs stability analysis to map the dynamical landscape, and discusses strategic implications for opinion manipulation.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

I study the impact of mixed contrarians on the opinion dynamics of an heterogenous population with conformists using Galam Majority Model. Activation of contrarians is a function of the ratio majority/minority in the local groups of discussion. Restricting the group size to 3, two types of contrarians are included in respective proportions $c_{3,0}$ for configurations with ratio 3 to 0 and $c_{2,1}$ for ratio 2 to 1. I then derive the explicit update Equation and obtained analytically the fixed points, their stability, and the resulting full two-dimensional landscape of the dynamics of opinion. Setting $c_{3,0} =c_{2,1} = c$ recovers the original results obtained with uniform contrarians. The findings allow for considering a wide spectrum of new disruptive strategies to secure either a majority/minority ending ensuring the opinion having the larger initial support to win, or a single attractor dynamics at fifty/fifty, which implies a random winner regardless of initial supports.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27738"></a>
### [Sampling two-dimensional spin systems with transformers](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27738v1)

**Authors:** Piotr Białas, Piotr Korcyl, Tomasz Stebel, Adam Stefański, Dawid Zapolski  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** disordered systems and neural networks · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27738v1>

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

**Summary.** This paper introduces a novel Transformer-based neural sampler called tVAN that uses patch-based generation and approximate probabilities to efficiently sample large 2D spin systems. It demonstrates significant improvements in sampling quality and scalability compared to previous neural network approaches, particularly for the Ising model at the critical point.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Developing an efficient Transformer-based neural sampler for large-scale classical spin systems, overcoming the computational inefficiency and scaling limitations of previous autoregressive models.

**Main result.** The proposed tVAN architecture can sample 2D Ising models up to 180x180 and 2D Edwards-Anderson spin glasses up to 64x64, achieving an Effective Sample Size 20 times larger than previous state-of-the-art neural samplers at the critical temperature.

**Method.** A Transformer Variational Autoregressive Network (tVAN) that generates groups of spins (patches) per step and utilizes an 'Approximate Probabilities' method to accelerate training and improve efficiency.

**Model / system.** The study focuses on 2D classical spin systems, specifically the 2D Ising model and the 2D Edwards-Anderson spin glass model, using a Hamiltonian based on nearest-neighbor interactions.

**Key observables.** Effective Sample Size (ESS), Variational Free Energy (Fq), and Relative Error in Free Energy Density.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Critical temperature for the Ising model, spin glass transition temperature, patch sizes (e.g., 2x4, 3x4), and system size L.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The Approximate Probabilities method is currently restricted to nearest-neighbor interactions, and the complexity analysis ignores element-wise operations and activation functions.

**Figures summary.** Figure 1 shows the tVAN architecture; Figure 2 illustrates patch-based generation; Figure 3 and 4 show training history (ESS vs. epochs/time) for various patch sizes and the impact of Approximate Probabilities; Figure 5 and 6 show ESS training history for the EA model; Appendix figures show scaling of training time and memory usage.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the tVAN architecture and patch-based generation, details the training process and the Approximate Probabilities method, presents performance results on Ising and Edwards-Anderson models, provides a complexity analysis of scaling with system size, and concludes with limitations and future directions.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Autoregressive Neural Networks based on dense or convolutional layers have recently been shown to be a viable strategy for generating classical spin systems. Unlike these methods, sampling with transformers is commonly considered to be computationally inefficient. In this work, we propose a novel approach to transformer-based neural samplers in which we generate not a single spin per step but groups of spins. As an additional improvement, we construct a model of approximated probabilities, further improving the efficiency of the algorithm. Despite our approach being computationally heavier than dense networks or CNN-based approaches, we were able to sample larger systems of up to $180 \times 180$ spins in case of the Ising model. The Effective Sample Size of our sampler is $\sim 20$ times larger than that of the previous state-of-the-art neural sampler when trained for the $128 \times 128$ Ising model at critical temperature. Finally, we also test our algorithm on the 2D Edwards-Anderson model, where we train $64\times 64$ spin systems.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27136"></a>
### [Stepping up enhanced rate calculations with EATR-flooding](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27136v1)

**Authors:** Nicodemo Mazzaferro, Willmor J Pena Ccoa, Pilar Cossio, Glen M. Hocky  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27136v1>  
**Analysis basis:** abstract only; PDF text extraction failed or PDF unavailable

**Summary.** This paper presents EATR-flooding, a new method for calculating rate constants in molecular simulations. It allows for more efficient and accurate rate estimation using quasi-static biasing schemes, making it broadly applicable to various enhanced sampling techniques.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The original EATR method for computing rate constants requires a time-dependent biasing potential, which limits its use in quasi-static biasing schemes like OPES or flooding.

**Main result.** The authors introduce EATR-flooding, a generalization that uses stepped-up biasing strengths across multiple simulations to estimate rates, providing an internal check for over-biasing and a more stable CV-quality factor.

**Method.** The method replaces time-dependent bias with a series of simulations with increasing biasing potential strengths (stepping up) and utilizes a learned CV-quality factor gamma.

**Model / system.** The method is demonstrated on a coarse-grained protein system and a fully atomistic cavity-ligand model.

**Key observables.** Rate constants of slow biomolecular processes and the CV-quality factor gamma.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The biasing potential strength and the CV-quality factor gamma.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The method assumes the applicability of the EATR framework to quasi-static biasing schemes and relies on the accuracy of the learned quality factor.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the limitation of the original EATR method, presents the new EATR-flooding approach, describes the implementation as an open-source Python library, and validates the method using protein and cavity-ligand models.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Several recent methods have shown that it is possible to compute rate constants of very slow biomolecular processes using simulations where a time-dependent bias is added along one or several collective variables (CVs). We previously reported the exponential average time-dependent rate (EATR) method, which can improve upon these approaches by accounting for how efficiently the external biasing potential modifies the observed rate using a learned CV-quality factor $γ$. This results in more accurate rate estimates using the same data when biasing a suboptimal coordinate. However, as formulated EATR depended on the biasing potential varying over time to properly determine the biasing efficiency, which limits the method's applicability to quasi-static biasing schemes such as ``flooding'' or on-the-fly probability enhanced sampling (OPES). Here, we present the EATR-flooding approach, which generalizes our method by replacing the need for a time dependent bias by instead varying (stepping up) the strength of the biasing potential across multiple sets of simulations. We implement this approach as an open-source Python library, and demonstrate that this approach is accurate without substantial loss of efficiency compared to standard EATR for a coarse-grained protein system, and also show good performance on a fully atomistic cavity-ligand model. Two additional appealing features of EATR-flooding are an internal check for over-biasing and the fact that only a single $γ$ parameter is predicted for a given choice of CVs, as compared to our earlier results where $γ$ empirically depended on biasing rate. Finally, we believe EATR-flooding applies not only to OPES simulations but more generally to CV biasing enhanced sampling approaches, making it broadly useful.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27222"></a>
### [The Great Chicken-and-Egg of Chemistry: Bonding vs. Stability Revisited](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27222v1)

**Authors:** Cherif F. Matta  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27222v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2604.27222_figures/2604.27222_fig1.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Fig. 1. Logical flow to chemical bonding descriptors starting from the of the Born–</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper provides a logical critique of how chemical bonding is conceptualized, arguing that 'bonds' are emergent patterns in the electron density rather than fundamental causes of stability. It aims to correct the 'category error' of treating derived descriptors as primitive physical entities in the molecular Hamiltonian. The work highlights the distinction between successful predictive models and true physical causation.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper addresses the logical fallacy in chemistry where chemical bonding and steric repulsion are treated as primitive causal agents of structural stability rather than derived descriptors of the quantum state.

**Main result.** The author demonstrates that bonding is an emergent, state-dependent descriptor that correlates with stability but does not constitute its fundamental cause, as the molecular Hamiltonian contains no bond operators.

**Method.** The paper employs a conceptual and logical analysis using frameworks such as QTAIM, the Born-Oppenheimer approximation, and Catastrophe Theory to evaluate the ontological status of chemical descriptors.

**Model / system.** The study focuses on molecular systems (including proteins and crystals) described by the non-relativistic molecular Hamiltonian involving electrons and nuclei.

**Key observables.** Electron density, bond paths, bond orders, Laplacian of the density, and energy density.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Stationary points of the potential energy surface, kinetic and potential energy densities, and the Born-Oppenheimer approximation.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The argument assumes the validity of the molecular Hamiltonian as the fundamental physical description of the system.

**Figures summary.** A graphical abstract illustrating the 'chicken-and-egg' problem of bonding and steric repulsion, and a figure depicting the logical flow from the Hamiltonian to derived descriptors.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by identifying the circular reasoning in chemical bonding, moves to an analysis of the molecular Hamiltonian and the derivation of descriptors, provides case studies like H-H bonding and protein stability, and concludes with a discussion on the hierarchy of chemical language and causation.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

The chemical bond is a central organizing concept in chemistry, yet it is absent from the molecular Hamiltonian and no "bond operator" exists. Bonding is therefore not a primitive physical entity but a derived descriptor emerging from the quantum state. The logical consequences of this observation are revisited. Statements such as "bonding stabilizes structure" when taken literally risk circular reasoning (petitio principii), whereby bonding is inferred from a stationary structure and then invoked as its cause. The same caution applies to concepts such as steric repulsion, which is also a derived descriptor. Bonding accompanies stable or metastable states and correlates with their properties without constituting their cause. Illustrative examples are drawn from QTAIM, non-covalent interaction (NCI) approach, protein structure, and hydrogen-hydrogen bonding. Causation, language, and the autonomy of chemistry are also briefly discussed. The aim is not at all to diminish the role of bonding, but to place it at the correct logical level, that is, as a powerful, state-dependent descriptor that organizes, classifies, and predicts chemical behavior without serving as its fundamental cause.

</details>

<a id="paper-2604.27189"></a>
### [The quantum group structure of long-range integrable deformations](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27189v1)

**Authors:** Koen Schouten, Marius de Leeuw  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2604.27189v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<details open><summary>📷 Fig 1</summary>

<img src="2604.27189_figures/2604.27189_page2.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 2</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 2</summary>

<img src="2604.27189_figures/2604.27189_page3.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 3</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 3</summary>

<img src="2604.27189_figures/2604.27189_page4.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 4</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 4</summary>

<img src="2604.27189_figures/2604.27189_page5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 5</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2604.27189_figures/2604.27189_page6.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>Low-resolution page preview, page 6</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** This paper provides a quantum group-theoretical description of long-range integrable deformations in spin chains. It reveals that these deformations arise from a twisting process that introduces non-associativity, with the Drinfeld associator acting as the key mechanism for encoding long-range interactions.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper aims to identify the underlying quantum group structure for long-range integrable deformations of spin chains, which had previously been unrecognized despite the known properties of their commuting charges.

**Main result.** The authors demonstrate that long-range deformations are obtained via a twist of the underlying quantum group, resulting in a non-associative algebra characterized by a non-trivial Drinfeld associator that encodes the long-range interaction terms.

**Method.** The study employs an algebraic framework using FRT-bialgebras, the quantum inverse scattering method, and a perturbative approach up to the first order in the deformation parameter, utilizing tools like the Sutherland equation and Drinfeld associators.

**Model / system.** The research focuses on arbitrary homogeneous Yang-Baxter integrable spin chains, including specific examples like the Heisenberg (XXX) and Haldane-Shastry spin chains, subject to long-range deformations generated by local, boost, and bilocal operators.

**Key observables.** Conserved charges (pairwise commuting charges), R-matrices, Lax operators, transfer matrices, and algebraic charge densities.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The deformation parameter (lambda) and the spectral parameters (u, v).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The results are provided only up to the first order in the deformation parameter, and the R-matrix is assumed to be analytic around the origin.

**Paper structure.** The paper begins by establishing the FRT-bialgebra framework and its duality with the Drinfeld-Jimbo approach, then introduces the twisting procedure to describe long-range deformations, proves the vanishing of the Drinfeld associator to establish the quantum group structure, and concludes with explicit constructions of Lax operators and connections to the Theta-morphism.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

Quantum integrable spin chains are known to possess a large family of long-range deformations generated by the local, boost and bilocal operators. Although these deformations are well-understood on the level of the pairwise commuting charges, the underlying quantum group structures had not yet been recognised. In this paper, we provide a quantum group-theoretical description for the family of long-range deformations of arbitrary homogeneous Yang-Baxter integrable spin chains up to first order in the deformation parameter. In particular, we show that the deformations are obtained via a twist of the algebraic structure of the underlying quantum group. This twisting results in a generally non-associative algebra that has a non-trivial Drinfeld associator. The Drinfeld associator is then shown to encode the information about the long-range interaction terms for the integrable spin chain. Moreover, the deformed quantum group is shown to contain a large perturbatively associative substructure, thus ensuring the perturbative integrability of the long-range model. The deformed quantum group provides explicit expressions for the Lax operators and R-matrices of the long-range deformed models, which manifestly satisfy the RLL relation and the Yang-Baxter equation up to first order in the deformation parameter. In order to derive the results, we introduce algebra elements that we call the algebraic charge densities. As a side result, we provide a conjecture for the explicit expressions of the undeformed charge densities in terms of these algebra elements.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2604.27746"></a>
### [The second altermagnet candidate in organic conductors: $κ$-(BEDT-TTF)$_2$$m$-HOOCC$_6$H$_4$SO$_3$](http://arxiv.org/abs/2604.27746v1)

**Authors:** Kohei Tokura, Takato Masuta, Kazushi Aoyama, Hiroki Akutsu, Yasuhiro Nakazawa, Scott S. Turner

<sub>FIG. 4. M-H plots of κ-m-SBA.</sub>

</details>

<details><summary>📷 Fig 5</summary>

<img src="2604.27746_figures/2604.27746_fig5.jpg" width="500"><br>
<sub>FIG. 5. The energy bands of κ-m-SBA.</sub>

</details>

**Summary.** The researchers synthesized a new organic conductor, kappa-m-SBA, which serves as the second known candidate for altermagnetism in organic salts. By combining experimental measurements with numerical simulations, they demonstrated that the material exhibits the spin-dependent band splitting characteristic of altermagnets. This finding expands the known library of organic materials with unique spin-orbit-like electronic structures without requiring heavy elements.

**Why it may be interesting.** not directly relevant

<details><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The identification of a new candidate for altermagnetism in organic conductors and explaining why the material kappa-m-SBA exhibits a canted antiferromagnetic transition instead of a spin liquid state.

**Main result.** The discovery of kappa-m-SBA as the second organic altermagnet candidate, demonstrating characteristic spin-dependent band splitting due to the interplay of AFM order and anisotropic electron hopping.

**Method.** The study combines electrocrystallization synthesis, SQUID magnetometry, and electrical resistivity measurements with first-principles (OpenMX) and tight-binding band calculations.

**Model / system.** A novel organic conductor, kappa-(BEDT-TTF)2m-HOOCC6H4SO3 (kappa-m-SBA), modeled using a Hubbard model on a dimerized, nearly equilateral triangular lattice.

**Key observables.** Magnetic susceptibility (chi-T), magnetization (M-H), electrical resistivity, spin-dependent band splitting, and the frustration parameter (t'/t).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Neel temperature (TN) = 14 K, transfer integrals (t, t', tb, tp, tq), Coulomb interaction (U = 0.54 eV), and Mott gap (0.22 eV).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The slightly canted magnetic structure is approximated as a collinear antiferromagnetic order to evaluate symmetry-driven altermagnetism.

**Figures summary.** Figure 5 shows energy band dispersion with spin splitting; Figure S8 shows the anionic layer crystal structure and dipole orientation; Figure S9 shows the classification of polar organic conductors.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the new material, details its synthesis and structural properties, analyzes its magnetic and electronic transport properties, and concludes with numerical calculations demonstrating altermagnetic signatures.

</details>

<details><summary>Abstract</summary>

We have developed a novel BEDT-TTF-based organic conductor, $κ$-(BEDT-TTF)$_2 m$-HOOCC$_6$H$_4$SO$_3$ ($κ$-$m$-SBA), and propose it as a candidate for altermagnet. Tight-binding band calculations of $κ$-$m$-SBA provide a $t'/t$ of 1.01 at 100 K, indicating that the spin structure is closely aligned to an equilateral triangle ($t'/t= 1$). While most $κ$-type BEDT-TTF-based salts become spin liquids due to the spin frustration caused by the triangular lattice, $κ$-$m$-SBA surprisingly shows a weak ferromagnetic transition at $T_\mathrm{N} = 14$ K due to a canted antiferromagnetic (AFM) spin structure. Until recently, $κ$-(BEDT-TTF)$_2$Cu[N(CN)$_2$]Cl ($κ$-Cl) was the only $κ$-type organic conductor known to exhibit this order, and it is also recognized as the first candidate for altermagnetism in organic conductors. This was theoretically predicted by Naka et al. in 2019, who demonstrated that $κ$-type organic conductors can be candidates for altermagnetism if they display such order. Consequently, $κ$-$m$-SBA can be considered the second candidate for altermagnetism in organic conductors. Furthermore, numerical calculations demonstrate a characteristic of altermagnets in $κ$-$m$-SBA, namely spin splitting of energy bands.

</details>
